- $C_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathsf{zk}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \ with \ a \ zero-knowledge \ encoding \ \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathsf{zk}};$   $\mathsf{sl} = (\mathsf{sl}, (\mathsf{sl}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}) \ where \ \mathsf{sl} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell} |, \ \mathsf{sl}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |, \ \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |.$ Define

$$\mathbf{sl'} \coloneqq (\times(\odot_k \mathsf{sl}), (\times(\mathsf{sl}_i))_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}_{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}^{\star}})_{j \in [k]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\mathrm{id}})_{j \in [k]}) \,.$$

Construction 6.3 is a IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl'}}$  with the following properties.

- Round complexity: k + 1.
- Prover communication (in field elements):  $k \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}}) + 1$ . Of these,  $k \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}}$  are sent as a single oracle message over alphabet  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^k$  and  $k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + 1$  are sent as non-oracle messages.
- Verifier queries: none (a queryless IOR).
- Prover time (in field operations):  $O(2^k \cdot \ell + t_{sl} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{sl_i} + k \cdot tenc(\mathcal{C}_{zk}))$ .
- Verifier time (in field operations):  $O(k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}})$ .
- Round-by-round security: For every  $\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0,1)$ , Construction 6.3 has RBR knowledge  $soundness \ with \ relaxation \ (\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}\equiv 2^k,\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}},\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}) \ \ and \ \ errors$

$$\left(\frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|},\;\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}},\delta)+\frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-(j-1)}},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}\right)_{j\in[k]}\right)\;.$$

The total extraction time is  $O(\sum_{j \in [k]} \mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}))$ .

• Zero-knowledge: If  $\operatorname{char}(\mathbb{F}) \neq 2$ ,  $\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \geq 2$ , and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  then, for every  $t \in \mathbb{N}^{1+n}$ , Construction 6.3 is HVZK for  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t, t_{\mathsf{zk}}, \dots, t_{\mathsf{zk}})}$  with error  $k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $\boldsymbol{t}$ .

#### <span id="page-36-1"></span>Construction 6.3.

- Inputs and notation. The verifier receives explicit input  $\mathbb{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), ((\boldsymbol{\mu}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}))$ and oracle access to implicit input  $y = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . In the honest case, the prover receives as input  $\mathbb{X}$  and  $\mathbb{Y}$  as well as witness  $\mathbb{W} = (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  such that  $(\mathbb{X}, \mathbb{Y}, \mathbb{W}) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{Z}^k}, \mathsf{S}^l}$ .
- Interaction phase.
  - 1. Sending masks. The prover sends  $s_1, \ldots, s_k \in \mathbb{F}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . In the honest case the prover samples  $s_1, \ldots, s_k \in \mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}[\mathtt{X}], \ r'_1, \ldots, r'_k \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \ \text{and sets} \ s_j \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(s_j, r'_j) \ \text{for each} \ j \in [k].$
  - 2. New target. The prover sends  $\tilde{\mu} \in \mathbb{F}$ . In the honest case the prover sets

$$\tilde{\mu} \coloneqq \sum_{\boldsymbol{b} \in \{0,1\}^k} \boldsymbol{s}_1(b_1) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_k(b_k).$$

{37}------------------------------------------------

- 3. Combination randomness. The verifier samples and sends  $\varepsilon \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ .
- 4. Sumcheck. Set  $\gamma := \emptyset$ . For  $j \in [k]$ :
  - (a) The prover sends  $\hat{h}_i \in \mathbb{F}^{<\max\{2,\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}\}}[X]$ . In the honest case

$$\hat{h}_{j}(\mathtt{X}) \coloneqq \begin{array}{l} \sum_{(b_{j+1}, \dots, b_k) \in \{0, 1\}} \boldsymbol{s}_{1}(\gamma_{1}) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_{j}(\mathtt{X}) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_{k}(b_{k}) \\ + \varepsilon \cdot \left( \langle \boldsymbol{f}(\boldsymbol{\gamma}, \mathtt{X}, \{0, 1\}^{k-j + \log \ell}), \odot_{j} \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}, (\boldsymbol{\gamma}, \mathtt{X})) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_{i}, \mathsf{sl}_{i}(\mathsf{st}_{i}) \rangle \right) \end{array}$$

where  $f(\gamma, X, \{0, 1\}^{k-j+\log \ell})$  denotes the linear polynomial (in X) obtained by performing a partial evaluation of f on  $(\gamma, X)$  and  $(\odot_j sl)(st, (\gamma, X))$  is well-defined by Equation 8.

- (b) The verifier samples and sends  $\gamma_j \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ . Set  $\gamma := \gamma || \gamma_j \in \mathbb{F}^j$ .
- Decision phase.
  - 1. The verifier checks that  $\hat{h}_1(0) + \hat{h}_1(1) = \varepsilon \cdot \mu + \tilde{\mu}$ .
  - 2. For every  $j \in \{2, \ldots, k\}$  the verifier checks that  $\hat{h}_j(0) + \hat{h}_j(1) = \hat{h}_{j-1}(\gamma_{j-1})$ .
- Output claims. The verifier sets new targets and states:
  - $-\mu' := \hat{h}_k(\gamma_k);$   $-\operatorname{st}' := ((\operatorname{st}, \gamma), \varepsilon);$   $-\forall i \in [n], \operatorname{st}'_i := (\operatorname{st}_i, \varepsilon) \text{ and } \forall j \in [k], \operatorname{st}'_{n+j} := \gamma_j;$   $-\forall i \in [n], \operatorname{st}'_{\circ,i} := \operatorname{st}_{\circ,i}, \ \mu'_i := \mu_i;$   $-\forall j \in [k], \operatorname{st}'_{\circ,n+j} := \mathbf{0}, \ \mu'_{n+j} := \mathbf{0}.$

The verifier outputs the following new explicit instance and implicit instance and in the honest case the prover outputs the following new witness:

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{z}' &\coloneqq ((\mu', \mathsf{st}', (\mathsf{st}'_i)_{i \in [n+k]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}'_i, \mathsf{st}'_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n+k]})\,, \\ \mathbf{y}' &\coloneqq (\mathsf{Fold}(f, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]}, (s_j)_{j \in [k]})\,, \\ \mathbf{w}' &\coloneqq (\mathsf{Fold}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), \mathsf{Fold}(\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\boldsymbol{s}_j, \boldsymbol{r}'_i)_{j \in [k]})\,. \end{split}$$

Completeness of Construction 6.3 follows by completeness of the sumcheck protocol and by Lemma 3.26.

## <span id="page-37-0"></span>6.1 Zero-knowledge

<span id="page-37-1"></span>**Lemma 6.4.** If  $\operatorname{char}(\mathbb{F}) \neq 2$ ,  $\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \geq 2$ , and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  then, for every  $t \in \mathbb{N}^{1+n}$ , Construction 6.3 is HVZK for  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t, t_{\mathsf{zk}}, \dots, t_{\mathsf{zk}})}$  with error  $k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity t.

*Proof.* Let  $Sim_{\mathcal{C}_{zk}}$  denote the simulator for  $Enc_{\mathcal{C}_{zk}}$ . We define the simulator S for the protocol.

 $\mathbf{S}^{y,\mathcal{D}}(\mathbf{x})$ :

- 1. Sample  $\varepsilon, \tilde{\mu} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$  and  $(\gamma_j)_{j \in [k]} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^k$ .
- 2. Sample  $(\hat{h}_j)_{j\in[k]}$  uniformly from  $\mathbb{F}^{<\max\{2,\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}\}}[X]$  conditioned on  $\hat{h}_1(0) + \hat{h}_1(1) = \varepsilon \cdot \mu + \tilde{\mu}$  and  $\forall j \in \{2,\ldots,k\}, \ \hat{h}_j(0) + \hat{h}_j(1) = \hat{h}_{j-1}(\gamma_{j-1}).$
- 3. Define  $\mathbf{z}'$  and  $\mathbf{y}'$  from  $(\mathbf{z}, \varepsilon, \boldsymbol{\gamma}, \tilde{\mu}, (\hat{h}_j)_{j \in [k]})$  as in the output-claims phase of Construction 6.3.

{38}------------------------------------------------

4. Since  $\mathcal{D}$  is non-adaptive (see Definition 4.7) there exists  $(\mathcal{D}_0, \mathcal{D}_1)$  such that

$$\mathcal{D}^{\mathsf{y}'}(\mathsf{x}') = \left[ \begin{array}{l} (\mathsf{st}, Q_{\mathsf{y}}, (Q_{s_j})_{j \in [k]}) \leftarrow \mathcal{D}_0(\mathsf{x}') \ \mathcal{D}_1(\mathsf{st}, \boldsymbol{a}_{\mathsf{y}}, (\boldsymbol{a}_{s_j})_{j \in [k]}) \end{array} \right].$$

- 5. Answer all queries in  $Q_y$  by forwarding to y (for queries to  $\mathsf{Fold}(f, \gamma)$  use the folding map), and denote the resulting answers by  $a_y$ . For every  $j \in [k]$ , set  $a_{s_j} \leftarrow \mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(Q_{s_j})$ .
- 6. Set out :=  $\mathcal{D}_1(\mathsf{st}, \boldsymbol{a}_{\mathsf{y}}, (\boldsymbol{a}_{s_j})_{j \in [k]})$  and output

$$\left((\varepsilon, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), (Q_{\mathtt{y}}, (Q_{s_j})_{j \in [k]}), ((\tilde{\mu}, \hat{h}_1, \dots, \hat{h}_k), \boldsymbol{a}_{\mathtt{y}}, (\boldsymbol{a}_{s_j})_{j \in [k]}), \mathsf{out}\right)$$
.

The simulator queries y exactly on  $Q_y$ , and by the distinguisher class bound this is at most t. We must show that for every  $(z, y, w) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}, \mathcal{C}_{zk}, sl}$  and every distinguisher  $\mathcal{D}$  in the stated class,

$$\Delta\left(\mathsf{View}(\mathbf{P},\mathbf{V},\mathcal{D},\mathbf{z},\mathbf{y},\mathbf{w}),\mathbf{S}^{\mathbf{y},\mathcal{D}}(\mathbf{z})\right) \leq k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}\,.$$

We prove this in two parts: first we show that the sumcheck-transcript component has the correct distribution, then we bound the oracle-answer simulation error.

• Sumcheck transcript. Fix verifier randomness  $(\varepsilon, \gamma)$ . Let  $\mathcal{T} \subseteq \mathbb{F}^{1+k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  be the affine subspace of tuples  $(\tilde{\mu}, \hat{h}_1, \dots, \hat{h}_k)$  satisfying the k verifier checks in Construction 6.3 (where we think of each  $\hat{h}_j$  as a list of  $\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}$  evaluations). Since each check imposes one independent linear constraint on the polynomial  $\hat{h}_j$ , the subspace  $\mathcal{T}$  has dimension  $1 + k \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} - 1)$ . The simulator samples uniformly from  $\mathcal{T}$  by construction.

In the honest execution, the masks  $(s_j)_{j\in[k]}$  are uniform in  $(\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[X])^k$ . The honest-prover formulas in Construction 6.3 define an affine function A:  $(\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[X])^k \to \mathbb{F}^{1+k\cdot\ell_{zk}}$  that maps  $(s_1,\ldots,s_k)\mapsto (\tilde{\mu},\hat{h}_1,\ldots,\hat{h}_k)$ . For  $\mathbf{z}\in (\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[X])^k$ , let  $L(\mathbf{z}):=A(\mathbf{z})-A(0)$  be its linear part, so that  $A(\mathbf{z})-A(\mathbf{z}')=L(\mathbf{z}-\mathbf{z}')$  for all  $\mathbf{z},\mathbf{z}'\in (\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[X])^k$ . Expanding the sumcheck formula,  $s_j$  is the only mask contributing non-constant (in X) terms to  $\hat{h}_j$ . Suppose  $\mathbf{z}:=(s_1,\ldots,s_k),\mathbf{z}':=(s_1',\ldots,s_k')$  satisfy  $A(\mathbf{z})=A(\mathbf{z}')$ , i.e.,  $\mathbf{z}-\mathbf{z}'\in \ker(\mathsf{L})$ . Since the non-constant coefficients of  $\hat{h}_j$  are  $2^{k-j}$  times those of  $s_j$  and  $\ker(\mathbb{F})\neq 2$ , each difference  $s_j-s_j'$  is some constant we denote by  $c_j\in\mathbb{F}$ . Such constants shift each  $\hat{h}_j$  by  $2^{k-j}\sum_{l=1}^k c_l$  and  $\tilde{\mu}$  by  $2^k\sum_{l=1}^k c_l$ . Therefore  $\ker(\mathsf{L})=\{(c_1,\ldots,c_k)\in\mathbb{F}^k:\sum_j c_j=0\}$  (formally,  $c_j$  is identified with the constant polynomial  $X\mapsto c_j$ ). Since  $\dim((\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[X])^k)=k\cdot\ell_{zk}$  and  $\dim\ker(\mathsf{L})=k-1$ , rank-nullity gives  $\dim\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{L})=1+k\cdot(\ell_{zk}-1)=\dim(\mathcal{T})$ . Also,  $\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{A})=A(0)+\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{L})$ , so  $\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{A})$  is an affine subspace with the same dimension as  $\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{L})$ . Because  $\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{A})\subseteq\mathcal{T}$  and both affine subspaces have dimension  $1+k\cdot(\ell_{zk}-1)$ , we get  $\operatorname{im}(\mathsf{A})=\mathcal{T}$ . Fix  $t\in\mathcal{T}$  and choose any  $\mathbf{z}_0\in\mathsf{A}^{-1}(t)$ . For any  $\mathbf{z}\in (\mathbb{F}^{<\ell_{zk}}[\mathsf{X}])^k$ ,

$$A(\mathbf{z}) = t \iff A(\mathbf{z}) - A(\mathbf{z}_0) = 0 \iff L(\mathbf{z} - \mathbf{z}_0) = 0 \iff \mathbf{z} - \mathbf{z}_0 \in \ker(L).$$

Hence  $A^{-1}(t) = \mathbf{z}_0 + \ker(\mathsf{L})$ , so  $|\mathsf{A}^{-1}(t)| = |\ker(\mathsf{L})| = |\mathbb{F}|^{k-1}$ . Therefore uniform masks induce the uniform distribution over  $\mathcal{T}$ .

{39}------------------------------------------------

• Oracle answers. Let  $Q_y$  and  $(Q_{s_j})_{j\in[k]}$  be the query sets output by  $\mathcal{D}_0$  in the simulator above. For  $j\in\{0,\ldots,k\}$ , define a hybrid  $H^{(j)}$  that answers  $Q_y$  from y, uses  $\mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  for  $Q_{s_l}$  with  $l\leq j$ , and uses honest values for l>j. Then  $H^{(0)}$  is the real experiment and  $H^{(k)}$  is the simulated one.

For each  $j \in [k]$ , hybrids  $H^{(j-1)}$  and  $H^{(j)}$  differ only in the oracle  $s_j$ . Since  $|Q_{s_j}| \leq t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ , by Definition 3.16 replacing honest answers  $s_j[Q_{s_j}]$  with  $\mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(Q_{s_j})$  changes statistical distance by at most  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . Summing over j gives a total simulation error of at most  $k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ .

By the first part, the simulator samples the sumcheck transcript with exactly the same distribution as in the real execution, hence the induced distribution of  $\mathbf{z}'$  and of the query sets output by  $\mathcal{D}_0$  is also the same. Therefore the differences in the simulation stem from the oracle-answer simulation which is bounded above (and applying  $\mathcal{D}_1$  to these answers to produce out). Thus  $\Delta\left(\mathsf{View}(\mathbf{P},\mathbf{V},\mathcal{D},\mathbf{z},\mathbf{y},\mathbf{w}),\mathbf{S}^{\mathbf{y},\mathcal{D}}(\mathbf{z})\right) \leq k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ .

# <span id="page-39-0"></span>6.2 Round-by-round security

**Lemma 6.5.** For every  $\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0, 1)$ , Construction 6.3 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $(\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}\equiv^{2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}, \tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}})$  and errors

$$\left(\frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|},\;\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}},\delta)+\frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-(j-1)}},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}\right)_{j\in[k]}\right)\;.$$

The total extraction time is  $O(\sum_{j \in [k]} \mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}))$ .

*Proof.* We give notation, describe the extractors, describe a state function, and finally we establish the RBR knowledge soundness errors (based on the extractor and state function).

**Notation.** Let  $\mathbf{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i, \mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$  and  $\mathbf{y} = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . A complete transcript of the protocol has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = ((s_j)_{j \in [k]}, \tilde{\mu}, \varepsilon, ((\hat{h}_j, \gamma_j))_{j \in [k]})$ . Given a partial transcript, we define the following symbols (these are defined whenever they can be derived from the partial transcript):

- $\boldsymbol{\gamma}^{(j)} = (\gamma_1, \dots, \gamma_j);$
- $f^{(j)} = \operatorname{Fold}(f, \gamma^{(j)})$ ; and
- $\mu^{(j)} = \hat{h}_j(\gamma_i)$  for j > 0 and  $\mu^{(0)} = \varepsilon \cdot \mu + \tilde{\mu}$ .

**Extractors.** We describe the round-by-round extractors from the last round to the first.

- 1. **Final round.**  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}||\gamma_k,\mathsf{w})$ :
  - (a) Parse w as  $((f, r), (\xi_i, r_i)_{i \in [n]}, (s_j, r'_j)_{j \in [k]})$ .
  - (b) Compute  $\bar{f} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r})$  and for every  $i \in [n]$  compute  $\bar{\xi_i} \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i})$  and for every  $j \in [k]$  compute  $\bar{s_j} \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s_j}, \boldsymbol{r'_j})$ .
  - (c) Output the round witness  $\mathbf{w}' \coloneqq \left( (\bar{f}, \mathbf{f}, \mathbf{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \mathbf{\xi}_i, \mathbf{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}_j, \mathbf{s}_j, \mathbf{r}'_j)_{j \in [k]} \right).$
- 2. Sumcheck round  $j \in [k]$ .  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || \gamma_j, \mathsf{w})$ :
  - (a) Parse was  $((\bar{f}^{(j)}, \mathbf{f}^{(j)}, \mathbf{r}^{(j)}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}_{j'}, \boldsymbol{s}_{j'}, \boldsymbol{r}'_{j'})_{j' \in [k]}).$
  - (b) Parse  $f^{(j)}$  and  $f^{(j-1)}$  from tr.

{40}------------------------------------------------

- (c) Computes the largest set  $S \subseteq [m]$  such that  $\bar{f}^{(j)}$  agrees with  $f^{(j)}$  and computes the erasure correction  $\bar{f}^{(j-1)} := \mathbf{E}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}}(f^{(j-1)}, S)$  (see Definition 3.9).
- (d) Compute  $(f^{(j-1)}, r^{(j-1)}) := \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}}^{-1}(\bar{f}^{(j-1)}).$
- (e) Output the round witness  $w' := ((\bar{f}^{(j-1)}, \mathbf{f}^{(j-1)}, \mathbf{r}^{(j-1)}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \mathbf{\xi}_i, \mathbf{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}_{j'}, \mathbf{s}_{j'}, \mathbf{r}'_{j'})_{j' \in [k]}).$
- 3. Combination randomness.  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|\mathbf{\varepsilon},\mathsf{w})$  outputs  $\mathsf{w}.$

The state function. We define a state function KState.

- 0. Initial transcript: We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\emptyset,\mathsf{w})=1$  if and only if  $(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\mathsf{w})\in \tilde{\mathcal{R}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$ .
- <span id="page-40-0"></span>1. **Combination randomness:** The transcript has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = \left((s_j)_{j \in [k]}, \tilde{\mu}\right)$  and the verifier samples  $\varepsilon \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || \varepsilon, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if

$$\mathsf{w} = \left((\bar{f}, \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}_j, \boldsymbol{s}_j, \boldsymbol{r}_j')_{j \in [k]}\right)$$

is such that

- $\Delta((f,\xi_1,\ldots,\xi_n,s_1,\ldots,s_k),(\bar{f},\bar{\xi}_1,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n,\bar{s}_1,\ldots,\bar{s}_k)) \leq (\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}},\ldots,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
- $\bullet \quad \bar{f} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), \ \forall \, i \in [n] \ \bar{\xi_i} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i}), \ \forall \, j \in [k] \ \bar{s}_j = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s_j}, \boldsymbol{r'_j});$
- $\forall i \in [n], \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
- $\sum_{\bm{b} \in \{0,1\}^k} \left( \bm{s}_1(b_1) + \dots + \bm{s}_k(b_k) \right) + \varepsilon \cdot \left( \langle \bm{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \bm{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \right) = \tilde{\mu} + \varepsilon \cdot \mu.$
- <span id="page-40-1"></span>2. **Sumcheck, round**  $j \in [k]$ : The transcript has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = \left((s_{j'})_{j' \in [k]}, \tilde{\mu}, \varepsilon, (\hat{h}_{j'}, \gamma_{j'})_{j' < j}, \hat{h}_{j}\right)$ . The verifier samples  $\gamma_{j} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || \gamma_{j}, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if

$$\mathsf{w} = \left( (\bar{f}^{(j)}, \boldsymbol{f}^{(j)}, \boldsymbol{r}^{(j)}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}_{j'}, \boldsymbol{s}_{j'}, \boldsymbol{r}'_{j'})_{j' \in [k]} \right)$$

is such that

- $\Delta((f^{(j)}, \xi_1, \dots, \xi_n, s_1, \dots, s_k), (\bar{f}^{(j)}, \bar{\xi}_1, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n, \bar{s}_1, \dots, \bar{s}_k)) \leq (\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}, \dots, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
- $\bullet \quad \bar{f}^{(j)} = \mathrm{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}}(\boldsymbol{f}^{(j)}, \boldsymbol{r}^{(j)}), \, \forall \, i \in [n] \; \bar{\xi}_i = \mathrm{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i), \, \forall \, j' \in [k] \; \bar{s}_{j'} = \mathrm{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s}_{j'}, \boldsymbol{r}'_{j'});$
- $\hat{h}_1(0) + \hat{h}_1(1) = \tilde{\mu} + \varepsilon \cdot \mu$  and  $\forall j' \in [j-1] \hat{h}_{j'+1}(0) + \hat{h}_{j'+1}(1) = \hat{h}_{j'}(\gamma_{j'});$
- $\forall i \in [n], \mathsf{sl}_{\diamond,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\diamond,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
- $\sum_{(b_j,...,b_k)\in\{0,1\}^{k-j}} (s_1(\gamma_1)+\cdots+s_k(b_k))+\varepsilon\cdot\left(\langle f^{(j)},\odot_j\mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st},\boldsymbol{\gamma})\rangle+\sum_{i\in[n]}\langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i,\mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i)\rangle\right)=\hat{h}_j(\gamma_j).$

Bounding the errors. We bound the RBR errors for the protocol.

1. Combination randomness. Let  $\mathsf{tr} = ((s_j)_{j \in [k]}, \tilde{\mu})$ . We show that:

$$\Pr\left[\exists\,\mathsf{w}:\ \, \frac{\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w})) = 0}{\land\,\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|\varepsilon,\mathsf{w}) = 1}\,\right] \leq \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}\,.$$

{41}------------------------------------------------

Fix w such that  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}||\varepsilon,\mathsf{w}) = 1$ . There are at most  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|$  choices of w such that the conditions in Item 1 hold. Since  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w}) = 0$  and  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}||\varepsilon,\mathsf{w}) = 1$  (and most of the items in state function are independent of  $\varepsilon$ ), it must be that either

$$\sum_{\boldsymbol{b} \in \{0,1\}^k} (\boldsymbol{s}_1(b_1) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_k(b_k)) \neq \tilde{\mu} \text{ or }$$
$$\langle \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \neq \mu.$$

By the polynomial identity lemma, Item 1 holds with probability  $\frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|}$ . Taking a union bound concludes this part.

2. Sumcheck randomness. Let  $\mathsf{tr} = \left( (s_{j'})_{j' \in [k]}, \tilde{\mu}, \varepsilon, (\hat{h}_{j'}, \gamma_{j'})_{j' < j}, \hat{h}_{j} \right)$ . We show that:

$$\begin{split} & \Pr\left[\exists\,\mathsf{w}: \begin{array}{l} \mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w})) = 0 \\ & \land\,\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}||\gamma_j,\mathsf{w}) = 1 \end{array}\right] \\ & \leq \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}},\delta) + \frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j+1}},\delta)|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|} \,. \end{split}$$

Consider the event  $E_1$  that for every  $S \subseteq [m]$  with  $|S| \ge (1 - \delta) \cdot m$  if there exists  $u \in \mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}$  such  $u(S) = f^{(j)}(S)$  then there exist  $v_0, v_1 \in \mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}$  such that  $(v_0, v_1)(S) = f^{(j-1)}(S)$ . Note that by Definition 3.14 we have that  $\Pr[\neg E_1] \le \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}, \delta)$ . The rest of the analysis is assuming that  $E_1$  holds.

Fix w such that  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} | \gamma_j, \mathsf{w}) = 1$ . Since  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w})) = 0$ , it must be that the conditions in Item 2 hold and thus  $\Delta(f^{(j)}, \bar{f}^{(j)}) \leq \delta$ . Therefore (since  $E_1$  holds) there are  $v_0, v_1 \in \mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}$  such that  $(v_0, v_1)(S) = f^{(j-1)}(S)$ . Since  $\Delta((1-\gamma_j) \cdot v_0 + \gamma_j \cdot v_1, \bar{f}) \leq \delta$  it must be that  $\bar{f}^{(j)} = (1-\gamma_j) \cdot v_0 + \gamma_j \cdot v_1$  and that  $v_0, v_1$  are the words that  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}$  outputs. Let  $\mathbf{f}_0, \mathbf{f}_1$  be the message (ignoring the randomness) underlying  $v_0, v_1$ . There are at most  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j+1}}, \delta)|$  such choices of  $\mathbf{f}_0, \mathbf{f}_1$ , and at most  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|$  choices for the mask-related messages in  $\mathsf{w}$ .

It must be that  $\hat{h}_j(0) + \hat{h}_j(1) = \hat{h}_{j-1}(\gamma_{j-1})$ , and thus it must be that

$$\begin{split} \hat{h}_{j}(\mathbf{X}) \neq \sum_{(b_{j+1}, \dots, b_{k}) \in \{0,1\}^{k-j-1}} (\boldsymbol{s}_{1}(\gamma_{1}) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_{j}(\mathbf{X}) + \dots + \boldsymbol{s}_{k}(b_{k})) + \\ \varepsilon \cdot \left( \langle \mathbf{X} \cdot \boldsymbol{f}_{0} + (1 - \mathbf{X}) \cdot \boldsymbol{f}_{1}, \odot_{j} \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}, (\boldsymbol{\gamma}, \mathbf{X})) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_{i}, \mathsf{sl}_{i}(\mathsf{st}_{i}) \rangle \right) \end{split}$$

as the right hand side sums to  $\hat{h}_{j-1}(\gamma_{j-1})$ , and if the left hand side did then  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathbb{x}, \mathbb{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w}) = 0$ , a contradiction. By the polynomial identity lemma, the probability this happens is bounded by  $\frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}{|\mathbb{F}|}$ . A union bound over the possible choices of  $\mathsf{w}$  concludes the lemma.

{42}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-42-0"></span>7 A non-succinct zero-knowledge protocol for constrained codes

We describe a zero-knowledge IOP for the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  (Definition 5.8). The IOP is non-succinct, and is used on small instances as a base case.

#### <span id="page-42-2"></span>**Theorem 7.1.** Fix the following:

- $n \in \mathbb{N}$ ;
- $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \Sigma^m \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota})^m$  has a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ ;
- $C_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \ has \ a \ zero-knowledge \ encoding \ \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}};$
- $\mathbf{sl} = (\mathbf{sl}, (\mathbf{sl}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}) \ where \ \mathbf{sl} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathbf{zk}}} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathbf{zk}}} |;$
- $t, t_{\mathsf{zk}} \in \mathbb{N}$  are repetition parameters.

Construction 7.2 is a 2-round IOPP for  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  with the following properties:

- Prover communication (in field elements):  $m \cdot \iota + n \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} + \ell + r + n \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + r_{\mathsf{zk}})$ . Of these,
  - $m \cdot \iota$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma$ ,
  - $-n \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^n$ , and
  - $-\ell + r + n \cdot (\ell_{zk} + r_{zk})$  are sent as non-oracle messages.
- $\bullet$  Query complexity: t queries to the first input oracle,  $t_{\sf zk}$  queries to the remaining oracles.
- Prover time (in field operations):  $O(\operatorname{tenc}(\mathcal{C}) + n \cdot \operatorname{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) + t_{\mathsf{sl}} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}})$ .
- Verifier time (in field operations):  $O(\operatorname{tenc}(\mathcal{C}) + n \cdot \operatorname{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{zk}) + t_{sl} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{sl_i} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{sl_{o,i}})$ .
- Round-by-round security: For every  $\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0,1)$ , Construction 7.2 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $\tilde{\mathcal{R}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  and errors

$$\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}, \delta) + \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \ \max\left\{(1 - \delta)^t, (1 - \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}\right\}\right).$$

The total extraction time is  $O(\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}) + n \cdot \mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}))$ .

• **Zero-knowledge:** If  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  is a t-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}}$  and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ , then Construction 7.2 is HVZK with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + n \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$ .

#### <span id="page-42-1"></span>Construction 7.2.

- Inputs and notation. The verifier receives explicit input  $\mathbf{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i, \mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$  and oracle access to implicit input  $\mathbf{y} = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . Here  $\mu \in \mathbb{F}$  and, for each  $i \in [n]$ ,  $\boldsymbol{\mu}_i \in \mathbb{F}^{t_i}$ . In the honest case, the prover receives  $\mathbf{x}$  and  $\mathbf{y}$  as well as witness  $\mathbf{w} = (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  such that  $(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathbf{w}) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}$ .
- Interaction phase.
  - 1. New masks. The prover sends  $g \in \Sigma^m$ ,  $s_1, \ldots, s_n \in \Sigma_{z_k}^{m_{z_k}}$ ,  $\mu' \in \mathbb{F}$ , and for each  $i \in [n]$  sends  $\mu'_i \in \mathbb{F}^{t_i}$ . In the honest case, the prover samples  $g \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ ,  $r' \in \mathbb{F}^r$  and for  $i \in [n]$  the prover samples  $s_i \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{z_k}}$  and  $r'_i \in \mathbb{F}^{r_{z_k}}$  and sets  $g \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g, r')$ ,  $\mu' \coloneqq \langle g, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle s_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle$  and for  $i \in [n]$  sets  $s_i \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{z_k}}(s_i, r'_i)$  and  $\mu'_i \coloneqq \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot s_i$ .
  - 2. Combination randomness. The verifier samples and sends  $\gamma \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ .
  - 3. **Answer.** The prover sends  $f^* \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ ,  $r^* \in \mathbb{F}^r$  and for  $i \in [n]$  sends  $\boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and  $\boldsymbol{r}_i^* \in \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . In the honest case,  $f^* \coloneqq \boldsymbol{g} + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{f}$  and  $r^* \coloneqq \boldsymbol{r}' + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{r}$  and, for  $i \in [n]$ ,  $\boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* \coloneqq \boldsymbol{s}_i + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i$  and  $\boldsymbol{r}_i^* \coloneqq \boldsymbol{r}_i' + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{r}_i$ .

{43}------------------------------------------------

- 4. **Spotcheck randomness.** The verifier samples and sends  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$  and  $y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \leftarrow [m_{\mathsf{zk}}]$ .
- **Decision phase.** The verifier computes  $f^* \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)$  and, for each  $i \in [n]$ , computes  $\xi_i^* \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\xi_i^*, r_i^*)$ ; then it performs the following checks.
  - Target checks:  $\begin{array}{l} \bullet \ \forall i \in [n], \ \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i' + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\mu}_i \\ \bullet \ \langle \boldsymbol{f}^*, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu' + \gamma \cdot \mu \end{array} .$
  - $-\mathcal{C}$  spot checks:  $\forall j \in [t], \ f^*(x_j) = g(x_j) + \gamma \cdot f(x_j).$
  - $-\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}} \text{ spot checks: } \forall i \in [n], \forall j \in [t_{\mathsf{zk}}], \ \xi_i^*(y_j) = s_i(y_j) + \gamma \cdot \xi_i(y_j).$

## <span id="page-43-0"></span>7.1 Zero-knowledge

**Lemma 7.3.** If  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  is a t-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}}$  and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ , then Construction 7.2 is HVZK with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + n \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$ .

*Proof.* We define the simulator.

 $\mathbf{S}^{y}(x)$ :

- 1. Parse  $\times$  as  $((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i, \mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$ , and recall that  $\mathsf{y}$  has the form  $(f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ .
- 2. Sample  $\gamma \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ ,  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$ , and  $y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \leftarrow [m_{\mathsf{zk}}]$ .
- 3. Set  $S := (x_1, \dots, x_t)$  and  $S' := (y_1, \dots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}})$ .
- 4. Query f[S] and, for every  $i \in [n]$ , query  $\xi_i[S']$ .
- 5. Sample  $g[S] \leftarrow \mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}}(S)$  and, for every  $i \in [n]$ , sample  $s_i[S'] \leftarrow \mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{7k}}}(S')$ .
- <span id="page-43-1"></span>6. Sample  $f^* \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$  and  $r^* \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^r$  such that  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)$  satisfies  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)(S) = g[S] + \gamma \cdot f[S]$ . (If no solution exists, abort.)
- <span id="page-43-2"></span>7. For every  $i \in [n]$ , sample  $\boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and  $\boldsymbol{r}_i^* \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  such that  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{r}_i^*)(S') = s_i[S'] + \gamma \cdot \xi_i[S']$ . (If no solution exists, abort.)
- 8. Set  $\mu' := \langle \boldsymbol{f}^*, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \gamma \cdot \mu$ .
- 9. For every  $i \in [n]$ , set  $\mu'_i := \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\mu}_i$ .
- 10. Output

$$\begin{pmatrix} \gamma, (x_1, \dots, x_t), (y_1, \dots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}), \\ \mu', (\boldsymbol{\mu}'_1, \dots, \boldsymbol{\mu}'_n), g[S], (s_1[S'], \dots, s_n[S']), \\ \boldsymbol{f}^*, \boldsymbol{r}^*, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \boldsymbol{\xi}_n^*), (\boldsymbol{r}_1^*, \dots, \boldsymbol{r}_n^*), \\ f[S], (\xi_1[S'], \dots, \xi_n[S']) \end{pmatrix}.$$

The simulator runs in polynomial time. This is straightforward except for Items 6 and 7. Since  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  are injective linear maps, there exist matrices  $G \in \mathbb{F}^{m \times (\ell + r)}$  and  $G_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \in \mathbb{F}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}} \times (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + r_{\mathsf{zk}})}$  such that  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(u) = G \cdot u$  and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(u) = G_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \cdot u$ . Sampling  $f^*$  and  $f^*$  such that  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, f^*)(S) = g[S] + \gamma \cdot f[S]$  is equivalent to sampling a solution to  $(G \cdot u)[S] = f$ , and similarly for each  $f^*$  with  $f^*$  with  $f^*$  both can be done in polynomial time.

Next we analyze the simulation error. We introduce an intermediate simulator  $\mathbf{S}_0^{y}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{w})$  that has access to the witness to the relation.

$$\mathbf{S}_0^{\mathrm{y}}(\mathrm{x},\mathrm{w}=(\boldsymbol{f},\boldsymbol{r},(\boldsymbol{\xi}_i,\boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i\in[n]})).$$

- 1. Sample  $\gamma \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ ,  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$ , and  $y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \leftarrow [m_{\mathsf{zk}}]$ .
- 2. Set  $S := (x_1, \ldots, x_t)$  and  $S' := (y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}})$ .

{44}------------------------------------------------

- 3. Sample  $\boldsymbol{g} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ ,  $\boldsymbol{r}' \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r}$ , and for every  $i \in [n]$  sample  $\boldsymbol{s}_{i} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and  $\boldsymbol{r}'_{i} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ .
- 4. Set  $g := \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g, r')$  and, for every  $i \in [n]$ ,  $s_i := \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(s_i, r'_i)$ .
- 5. Set

$$\bm{f}^* \coloneqq \bm{g} + \gamma \cdot \bm{f} \,, \qquad \qquad \bm{r}^* \coloneqq \bm{r}' + \gamma \cdot \bm{r} \,, \ \forall \, i \in [n]: \, \bm{\xi}_i^* \coloneqq \bm{s}_i + \gamma \cdot \bm{\xi}_i \,, \qquad \qquad \bm{r}_i^* \coloneqq \bm{r}_i' + \gamma \cdot \bm{r}_i \,.$$

6. Set

$$\mu' \coloneqq \langle \boldsymbol{g}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{s}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \,,$$
 $\forall \, i \in [n]: \; \boldsymbol{\mu}_i' \coloneqq \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{s}_i \,.$ 

7. Output

$$\begin{pmatrix} \gamma, (x_1, \dots, x_t), (y_1, \dots, y_{t_{z_k}}), \\ \mu', (\boldsymbol{\mu}'_1, \dots, \boldsymbol{\mu}'_n), g[S], (s_1[S'], \dots, s_n[S']), \\ \boldsymbol{f}^*, \boldsymbol{r}^*, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \boldsymbol{\xi}_n^*), (\boldsymbol{r}_1^*, \dots, \boldsymbol{r}_n^*), \\ f[S], (\xi_1[S'], \dots, \xi_n[S']) \end{pmatrix}.$$

Conditioned on g[S] and  $(s_i[S'])_{i\in[n]}$ , the sampling of  $(f^*, r^*)$  and  $(\xi_i^*, r_i^*)$  in  $\mathbf{S}_0$  is uniform over the solution sets of the linear systems in Item 6. Therefore the only statistical gap between  $\mathbf{S}$  and  $\mathbf{S}_0$  comes from simulating g[S] and  $(s_i[S'])_{i\in[n]}$ : by Definition 3.16 and a union bound over these n+1 codewords, this gap is at most  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + n \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{zk}}$ . The distribution of  $\mathbf{S}_0$  is identical to the real view, so the simulation error is at most  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + n \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{zk}}$ .

## <span id="page-44-0"></span>7.2 Round-by-round knowledge soundness

**Lemma 7.4.** For every  $\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0, 1)$ , Construction 7.2 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}^{\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and errors

$$\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}, \delta) + \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \ \max\left\{(1 - \delta)^t, (1 - \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}\right\}\right).$$

The total extraction time is  $O(\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}) + n \cdot \mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}))$ .

*Proof.* We give notation, describe the extractors, describe a state function, and finally we establish the RBR knowledge soundness errors (based on the extractor and state function).

**Notation.** Let  $x = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, \mathsf{st}_1, \dots, \mathsf{st}_n), (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i, \mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$  and  $y = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . A complete transcript of the protocol has the form

$$\mathsf{tr} = \left(g, s_1, \dots, s_n, \mu', \mu'_1, \dots, \mu'_n, \gamma, f^*, r^*, (\xi_i^*, r_i^*)_{i \in [n]}, x_1, \dots, x_t, y_1, \dots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}\right).$$

**Extractor.** We describe the round-by-round extractors from the last round to the first.

#### 1. Spotcheck randomness.

- (a) Parse the transcript to obtain  $f^*$ ,  $r^*$ , and  $(\xi_i^*, r_i^*)_{i \in [n]}$ .
- (b) Compute  $\bar{f}^* := \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)$  and  $(\bar{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n^*) := \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n}}((\xi_1^*, \dots, \xi_n^*), (r_1^*, \dots, r_n^*))$ .

{45}------------------------------------------------

- (c) Outputs the round witness  $\mathbf{w} \coloneqq (\bar{f}^*, \mathbf{f}^*, \mathbf{r}^*, (\bar{\xi}_i^*, \mathbf{\xi}_i^*, \mathbf{r}_i^*)_{i \in [n]}).$
- 2. Combination randomness.
  - (a) Parse w as  $(\bar{f}^*, f^*, r^*, (\bar{\xi}_i^*, \xi_i^*, r_i^*)_{i \in [n]})$ .
  - (b) Let  $S \subseteq [m]$  be the largest set on which  $\bar{f}^*$  agrees with  $g + \gamma \cdot f$ .
  - (c) Use the erasure corrector  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathcal{C}}$  for  $\mathcal{C}$  to obtain codewords  $\bar{f}, \bar{g}$  from f(S), g(S) and decode them to (f, r), (g, r').
  - (d) Let  $S' \subseteq [m_{zk}]$  be the largest set on which  $(\bar{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n^*)$  agrees with  $(s_1 + \gamma \cdot \xi_1, \dots, s_n + \gamma \cdot \xi_n)$ .
  - (e) For every  $i \in [n]$ , use the erasure corrector  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  for  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  to obtain codewords  $\bar{\xi}_i, \bar{s}_i$  from  $\xi_i(S'), s_i(S')$  and decode them to  $(\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i), (\boldsymbol{s}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i')$ .
  - (f) Output the round witness  $w := (f, r, g, r', (\xi_i, r_i, s_i, r'_i)_{i \in [n]}).$
- 3. Final extraction.
  - (a) Parse w as  $(f, r, g, r', (\xi_i, r_i, s_i, r'_i)_{i \in [n]})$ .
  - (b) Compute  $\bar{f} := \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r})$  and for every  $i \in [n]$  compute  $\bar{\xi_i} := \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i})$ .
  - (c) Output  $(w, y^*)$  where  $w := (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  and  $y^* := (\bar{f}, (\bar{\xi}_i)_{i \in [n]})$ .

The state function. We define a state function KState.

- 0. **Initial transcript:** We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\emptyset,\mathsf{w})=1$  if and only if  $(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\mathsf{w})\in \tilde{\mathcal{R}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$ .
- 1. Combination randomness: The transcript is  $\mathsf{tr} = (g, s_1, \dots, s_n, \mu', \boldsymbol{\mu}_1', \dots, \boldsymbol{\mu}_n')$  and the verifier samples  $\gamma \leftarrow \mathbb{F}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} \| \gamma, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if  $\mathsf{w} = (\bar{f}^*, \boldsymbol{f}^*, \boldsymbol{r}^*, (\bar{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{r}_i^*))$  such that all of following hold:
  - (a)  $\bar{f}^* = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)$  and  $(\bar{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n^*) = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{Z}_n}^{\equiv n}}((\xi_1^*, \dots, \xi_n^*), (r_1^*, \dots, r_n^*));$
  - (b)  $\Delta(g+\gamma\cdot f,\bar{f}^*)\leq \delta$  and  $\Delta((s_1+\gamma\cdot\xi_1,\ldots,s_n+\gamma\cdot\xi_n),(\bar{\xi}_1^*,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n^*))\leq \delta_{\mathsf{zk}};$
  - (c) the following both hold

$$\begin{aligned} \langle \boldsymbol{f}^*, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu' + \gamma \cdot \mu \,, \ \forall \, i \in [n]: \; \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^* = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i' + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\mu}_i \,. \end{aligned}$$

2. **Spotcheck randomness:** The transcript is  $\mathsf{tr} = (g, (s_i)_{i \in [n]}, \mu', (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i')_{i \in [n]}, \gamma, \boldsymbol{f}^*, \boldsymbol{r}^*, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{r}_i^*)_{i \in [n]})$  and the verifier samples  $x_1, \ldots, x_t$  and  $y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} \| (x_1, \ldots, x_t, y_1, \ldots, y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}), \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if  $\mathsf{w} = \emptyset$  and the verifier accepts.

**Bounding the errors.** We bound the RBR errors for the protocol.

1. Combination randomness. We show that

$$\begin{split} &\Pr_{\gamma} \left[ \exists \, \mathsf{w} : \begin{array}{l} \mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w})) = 0 \\ & \land \, \mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || \gamma, \mathsf{w}) = 1 \end{array} \right] \\ &\leq \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}, \delta) + \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \end{array}.$$

Let  $E_1$  be the event that for every  $S \subseteq [m]$  with  $|S| \ge (1 - \delta) \cdot m$  if there exists a codeword  $u \in \mathcal{C}$  such that  $u(S) = (g + \gamma \cdot f)(S)$  then there exist  $u_g, u_f \in \mathcal{C}$  such that  $u_g(S) = g(S)$  and

{46}------------------------------------------------

 $u_f(S) = f(S)$ . Similarly, let  $E_2$  be the event that for every  $S' \subseteq [m_{zk}]$  with  $|S'| \ge (1 - \delta_{zk}) \cdot m_{zk}$  if there exists a codeword  $u' \in \mathcal{C}_{zk}^{\equiv n}$  such that  $u'(S') = (s_1 + \gamma \cdot \xi_1, \dots, s_n + \gamma \cdot \xi_n)(S')$  then there exist codewords  $(u_{\xi,1}, \dots, u_{\xi,n})$  in  $\mathcal{C}_{zk}^{\equiv n}$  such that  $u_{\xi,i}(S') = \xi_i(S')$  for all  $i \in [n]$ . By Definition 3.14,  $\Pr[\neg E_1] \le \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}, \delta)$  and  $\Pr[\neg E_2] \le \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{zk}^{\equiv n}, \delta_{zk})$ . We condition on  $E_1 \wedge E_2$  in the rest of the analysis.

Fix  $\mathbf{w} = (\bar{f}^*, \mathbf{f}^*, \mathbf{r}^*, (\bar{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{r}_i^*)_{i \in [n]})$  such that  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} \| \gamma, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  and let

$$(\boldsymbol{f},\boldsymbol{r},\boldsymbol{g},\boldsymbol{r}',(\boldsymbol{\xi}_i,\boldsymbol{r}_i,\boldsymbol{s}_i,\boldsymbol{r}'_i)_{i\in[n]})=\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\boldsymbol{\mathtt{z}},\boldsymbol{\mathtt{y}},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w})$$

denote the output of the extractor on w.

By  $E_1$  and  $E_2$  and the definition of the extractor  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}$  there are at most  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|$  possible choices for w. This is because:

- Since KState(x, y, tr||\gamma, w) = 1 it must be that  $\Delta(g + \gamma \cdot f, \bar{f}^*) \leq \delta$  and similarly for  $i \in [n]$  it must be that  $\Delta(s_i + \gamma \cdot \xi_i, \bar{\xi}_i^*) \leq \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}$ . Thus, by  $E_1, E_2$  there must exists sets S and S' with  $|S| \geq (1 \delta) \cdot m$  and  $|S'| \geq (1 \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}}$  such that (f, g) agrees with the interleaved code  $\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}$  on S and  $(\xi_1, \ldots, \xi_n, s_1, \ldots, s_n)$  agrees with the interleaved code  $\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}_{\mathsf{zk}}$ .
- The extractor by definition outputs the messages underlying the interleaved code, and thus there can be at most  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{zk}^{\equiv 2 \cdot n}, \delta_{zk})|$  such choices.
- Further, it must be that  $f^* = g + \gamma \cdot f$ . For any  $x \in S$  it holds that  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f^*, r^*)(x) = f^*(x) = g(x) + \gamma \cdot f(x) = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g, r')(x) + \gamma \cdot \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(f, r)(x) = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g + \gamma \cdot f, r' + \gamma \cdot r)(x)$ . Since the two codewords agrees on a set of size  $(1 \delta) \cdot m \geq (1 \delta(\mathcal{C})) \cdot m$  they must be the same codeword, and since the encoding is injective it must in fact be that  $f^* = g + \gamma \cdot f$  and  $r^* = r' + \gamma \cdot r$ . A similar fact also holds for the  $\xi_i, s_i$ .

Suppose that  $\mathsf{KState}(x, y, \mathsf{tr}, \mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(x, y, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w})) = 0$ , it must then be that either

$$\langle \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \neq \mu \text{ or}$$
  
$$\exists i \in [n] : \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i \neq \boldsymbol{\mu}_i.$$

In either case, the probability over a choice of  $\gamma$  that

$$\langle g + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{s}_i + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu' + \gamma \cdot \mu \text{ and}$$
  
 $\forall i \in [n]: \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot (\boldsymbol{s}_i + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i) = \boldsymbol{\mu}'_i + \gamma \cdot \boldsymbol{\mu}_i.$ 

is at most  $\frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|}$ . Since, as noted before,  $f^* = g + \gamma \cdot f$  and for  $i \in [n]$  it holds that  $\xi_i^* = s_i + \gamma \cdot \xi_i$ , this implies that  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w}) = 0$ . Taking a union bound over all possible witnesses yields the bound above.

## 2. Spotcheck randomness. We show that

$$\Pr_{(x_1,\ldots,x_t,y_1,\ldots,y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}})} \left[ \begin{array}{l} \mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr},\emptyset)) = 0 \\ \wedge \; \mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{x},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr} \| (x_1,\ldots,x_t,y_1,\ldots,y_{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}),\emptyset) = 1 \end{array} \right] \leq \max \left\{ (1-\delta)^t, (1-\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \right\} \, .$$

Write  $(\bar{f}^*, \boldsymbol{f}^*, \boldsymbol{r}^*, (\bar{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i^*, \boldsymbol{r}_i^*)_{i \in [n]})$  for  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \emptyset)$ . If the linear constraints in the decision phase fail, the verifier rejects regardless of the sampled points. Otherwise, either  $\Delta(g + \gamma \cdot f, \bar{f}^*) > \delta$ 

{47}------------------------------------------------

or  $\Delta((s_1 + \gamma \cdot \xi_1, \dots, s_n + \gamma \cdot \xi_n), (\bar{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n^*)) > \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}$ . In the first case,  $\Delta(g + \gamma \cdot f, \bar{f}^*) > \delta$ , then with probability at most  $(1 - \delta)^t$  all  $x_j$  fall in the agreement set, and the  $\mathcal{C}$ -local checks pass. Similarly, if  $\Delta((s_1 + \gamma \cdot \xi_1, \dots, s_n + \gamma \cdot \xi_n), (\bar{\xi}_1^*, \dots, \bar{\xi}_n^*)) > \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}$ , then with probability at most  $(1 - \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  all  $y_j$  avoid disagreement positions and the  $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -local checks pass.

{48}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-48-0"></span>8 A sublinear zero-knowledge IOP for constrained codes

<span id="page-48-2"></span>We prove Theorem 1 by composing the IOR of Theorem 6.2 and the 2-round IOPP of Theorem 7.1.

**Theorem 8.1.** Consider the following ingredients:

- $n, k \in \mathbb{N}$ ;
- $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \Sigma^m \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota})^m$  with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ ;
- $C_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \text{ with a zero-knowledge encoding } \mathsf{Enc}_{C_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}};$
- $\mathbf{sl} = (\mathbf{sl}, (\mathbf{sl}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}) \ where \ \mathbf{sl} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |;$
- $t, t_{\mathsf{zk}} \in \mathbb{N}$  are repetition parameters.

Construction 8.2 is an IOPP for  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  with the following parameters.

- Round complexity: k + 3.
- Prover communication (in field elements):  $O(k \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}) + m \cdot \iota + (n+k) \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} + \ell + r + (n+k) \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + r_{\mathsf{zk}}))$ . Of these  $m \cdot \iota$  are sent as an oracle with alphabet  $\Sigma$ ,  $(n+2 \cdot k) \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}$  are sent as an oracle with alphabet  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{n+2 \cdot k}$ , and  $k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \ell + r + (n+k) \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + r_{\mathsf{zk}})$  are sent as non-oracle messages.
- Verifier queries: the verifier makes t oracle queries to f over alphabet  $\Sigma^{2^k}$  and, for each mask oracle in the protocol (namely the n masks from the instance together with the k masks introduced by the sumcheck IOR), it makes at most  $t_{zk}$  oracle queries over alphabet  $\Sigma_{zk}$ .
- Prover time (in field operations):  $O(2^k \cdot \ell + t_{\mathsf{sl}} + k \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) + k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}) + (n+k) \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}_{\ell-k}}^{\star}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{id}}}).$
- $\begin{array}{ll} \bullet & \textit{Verifier time (in field operations): } O(2^k \cdot t + k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}) + (n+k) \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) + t_{\odot_k \mathsf{sl}} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}}} \\ & \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{d}}} \\ \\ & + k \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}$
- Round-by-round security: For every  $\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0,1)$ , Construction 8.2 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and errors:

$$\left( \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \left( \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}, \delta) + \frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-(j-1)}}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|} \right)_{j \in [k]},$$

$$\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}, \delta) + \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+k}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2(n+k)}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \max\left\{ (1 - \delta)^t, (1 - \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \right\} \right).$$

The total extraction time is  $O\left(\sum_{j\in[k]}\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}})+(n+k)\cdot\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}})\right)$ .

• **Zero-knowledge:** If  $\operatorname{char}(\mathbb{F}) \neq 2$ ,  $\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \geq 2$ ,  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  is a t-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}}$ , and  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ , then Construction 8.2 is HVZK with error  $2^k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + (n+2k) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$ .

## <span id="page-48-1"></span>Construction 8.2.

- Inputs. The verifier receives explicit input  $\mathbf{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), ((\boldsymbol{\mu}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}))$  and oracle access to implicit input  $\mathbf{y} = (f, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . In the honest case, the prover receives as input  $\mathbf{x}$  and  $\mathbf{y}$  as well as witness  $\mathbf{w} = (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  such that  $(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathbf{w}) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{rk}}, \mathsf{sl}}$ .
- Interaction phase.

{49}------------------------------------------------

- Sumcheck IOR. The prover and verifier run the zero-knowledge sumcheck IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$  in Construction 6.3, leading to:

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{z}' \coloneqq \left( (\mu', \mathsf{st}', (\mathsf{st}'_i)_{i \in [n+k]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}'_i, \mathsf{st}'_{\circ, i})_{i \in [n+k]} \right), \\ \mathbf{y}' \coloneqq \left( \mathsf{Fold}(f, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]}, (s_j)_{j \in [k]} \right), \\ \text{(in the honest case)} \quad \mathbf{w}' \coloneqq \left( \mathsf{Fold}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), \mathsf{Fold}(\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{\gamma}), (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\boldsymbol{s}_j, \boldsymbol{r}'_j)_{j \in [k]} \right), \\ \mathbf{sl}' \coloneqq \left( \times (\odot_k \mathsf{sl}), (\times (\mathsf{sl}_i))_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}^{\star}_{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}}})_{j \in [k]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\circ, i})_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{id}})_{j \in [k]} \right). \end{split}$$

Above  $\gamma \in \mathbb{F}^k$  is the randomness sampled during the sumcheck protocol.

- Non-succinct IOPP. The prover and verifier run the IOPP for the relation  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl'}}$  in Construction 7.2 on  $(\varkappa', y', \varkappa')$ , with repetition parameters  $(t, t_{\mathsf{zk}})$ .

Proof of Theorem 8.1. Let  $\mathsf{IOR}_1$  be Construction 6.3 and let  $\mathsf{IOR}_2$  be Construction 7.2 instantiated on  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl'}}$  with n+k mask oracles. Construction 8.2 is the concatenation  $\mathsf{IOR}_2 \circ \mathsf{IOR}_1$ .

The stated round complexity, prover communication, verifier queries, prover/verifier time, and round-by-round errors are obtained by combining the corresponding bounds from Theorems 6.2 and 7.1. We now establish HVZK:

- By Theorem 7.1,  $\mathsf{IOR}_2$  has a simulator  $\mathbf{S}_2$  with error  $\epsilon_2 \coloneqq \zeta_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}} + (n+k) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n+k]})$ . In the concatenated protocol, the first-oracle queries handled through  $\mathbf{S}_2$  are induced by queries to the original oracle f, which is a codeword of  $\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}$ .
- Let  $t := (t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$ , and define  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_2}$  as in Definition 4.4, i.e.,  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_2}^{\mathsf{y}}(\cdot) := \mathbf{S}_2^{\mathsf{y}}(\cdot)$ . By the query bound of  $\mathbf{S}_2$ ,  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_2}$  makes at most t queries to the first oracle of  $\mathsf{y}'$ , at most  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  queries to each of the next n mask oracles, and at most  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  queries to each of the k new mask oracles. Hence  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_2} \in \mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t,(t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{j \in [k]})}$ . By Theorem 6.2,  $\mathsf{IOR}_1$  is  $\mathsf{HVZK}$  for this distinguisher via a simulator  $\mathbf{S}_1$  with error  $\epsilon_1 := k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$ .
- Apply Theorem 4.5 with  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{start}} \coloneqq \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C} \equiv 2^k, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}, \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{int}} \coloneqq \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}'}, \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{fin}} \coloneqq \mathcal{R}_{\mathsf{triv}}$ . The composed protocol is HVZK with query complexity  $(t, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{i \in [n]})$  and error at most  $\epsilon_1 + \epsilon_2 = \zeta_{\mathcal{C} \equiv 2^k} + (n+2k) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . By Claim 3.23,  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C} \equiv 2^k} \leq 2^k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}}$ , and therefore

$$\epsilon_1 + \epsilon_2 \le 2^k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}} + (n+2k) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}.$$

In sum Construction 8.2 is an IOPP with HVZK simulation error  $2^k \cdot \zeta_c + (n+2k) \cdot \zeta_{c-1}$ .

{50}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-50-0"></span>9 Zero-knowledge code-switching

We introduce an honest-verifier zero-knowledge code-switching protocol. To do so, we first introduce the variant of out-of-domain samples that we use in Section 9.1, the notion of private zero-evaders in Section 9.2, and a measure of the code-switching efficiency in Section 9.3.

# <span id="page-50-1"></span>9.1 Out-of-domain samples

We refine the notion of out-of-domain samples for a linear code (see [BGKS20] and their later uses in [ACFY24; ACFY25; BCFW25]) to account for zero-knowledge encodings. Specifically, in this paper we need to ensure that the "disagreement" is on the message part of the zero-knowledge code and not (only) the randomness part.

<span id="page-50-3"></span>**Lemma 9.1.** Let  $C \subseteq \Sigma^m$  be an  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_C \colon \mathbb{F}^\ell \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ ,  $f \in \Sigma^m$  be a word, and  $\delta \in [0,1]$  be a distance parameter. Let  $\mathsf{ze} \colon D_{\mathsf{ze}} \to \mathbb{F}^{t \times \ell}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$  (Definition 3.3). Then,

$$\Pr_{\rho \leftarrow D_{\mathsf{ze}}} \left[ \begin{array}{l} \exists \, u, v \in \Lambda(\mathcal{C}, f, \delta) \, \, s.t. \\ \boldsymbol{u} \neq \boldsymbol{v} \, \wedge \, \operatorname{ze}(\rho) \cdot \boldsymbol{u} = \operatorname{ze}(\rho) \cdot \boldsymbol{v} \\ where \, (\boldsymbol{u}, \boldsymbol{r}) \coloneqq \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}^{-1}(u), \, \, (\boldsymbol{v}, \boldsymbol{r}') \coloneqq \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}^{-1}(v) \end{array} \right] \leq \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}, \delta)|^2}{2} \cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}} \, .$$

Proof. Let  $u, v \in \Lambda(\mathcal{C}, f, \delta)$  be distinct codewords and  $(\boldsymbol{u}, \boldsymbol{r}) \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}^{-1}(u)$  and  $(\boldsymbol{v}, \boldsymbol{r}') \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}^{-1}(v)$ . We consider two cases: (i) if  $\boldsymbol{u} = \boldsymbol{v}$ , we are done; (ii) if  $\boldsymbol{u} \neq \boldsymbol{v}$ , since  $\mathsf{ze}$  is a zero-evader  $\mathsf{ze}(\rho) \cdot \boldsymbol{u} = \mathsf{ze}(\rho) \cdot \boldsymbol{v}$  with probability at most  $\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$ . The bound follows by taking a union bound over the at most  $\binom{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C},\delta)|}{2}$  distinct pairs of codewords in  $\Lambda(\mathcal{C}, f, \delta)$ .

#### <span id="page-50-2"></span>9.2 Private zero-evaders

We consider zero-evaders with a *privacy guarantee*: the inner product with a vector consisting of a private portion and a random portion reveals little or no information about the private portion.

**Definition 9.2.** A zero-evader ze:  $D_{ze} \to \mathbb{F}^{t \times \ell}$  is  $(r, \zeta_{ze})$ -private if there exists a simulator  $\mathbf{S}_{ze}$  such that for every  $\mathbf{f} \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell-r}$  the following two distributions have statistical distance at most  $\zeta_{ze}$ :

$$\left\{ \begin{array}{ll} (\rho, \boldsymbol{y}) & \rho \leftarrow D_{\sf ze}, \boldsymbol{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^r \ \boldsymbol{y} = {\sf ze}(\rho) \cdot \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{f} \ \boldsymbol{r} \end{array} \right\} \ and \ \boldsymbol{\bf S}_{\sf ze} \, .$$

By considering the all-zero zero-evader, one can see that there are zero-evaders with good privacy guarantees but trivial zero-evading error. In fact any zero-evader can be modified to have *perfect* privacy guarantees while essentially preserving the zero-evading error.

**Lemma 9.3.** Let  $ze: D_{ze} \to \mathbb{F}^{t \times \ell}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{zero}$ . For every  $r \in \mathbb{N}$  with  $r \geq t$ , there exists a zero-evader  $ze': D'_{ze} \to \mathbb{F}^{t \times (\ell+r)}$  with error  $\max\{\varepsilon_{zero}, \frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|^t-1}\}$  that is (r, 0)-private.

*Proof.* Let

$$\mathcal{M}_{t,r} \coloneqq \left\{ \boldsymbol{M} \in \mathbb{F}^{t \times r} \; : \; \text{the columns of } \boldsymbol{M} \; \text{span} \; \mathbb{F}^t \right\}.$$

Define  $D'_{ze} := D_{ze} \times \mathcal{M}_{t,r}$  and

$$\mathsf{ze}'(\rho, \boldsymbol{M}) \coloneqq \left[\mathsf{ze}(\rho), \boldsymbol{M}\right].$$

{51}------------------------------------------------

**Privacy error.** Fix any  $f \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ . Let  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{ze}'}$  be the simulator that samples  $(\rho, \mathbf{M}) \leftarrow D'_{\mathsf{ze}}$  and  $\mathbf{r} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r}$ . Let  $\mathbf{t}_{\rho} := \mathsf{ze}(\rho) \cdot \mathbf{f} \in \mathbb{F}^{t}$ . The sample from the real distribution is

$$((\rho,\bm{M}),\bm{y}) \quad \text{where} \quad \bm{y} = \mathsf{ze}'(\rho,\bm{M}) \cdot \begin{bmatrix} \bm{f} \\ \bm{r} \end{bmatrix} = \bm{t}_\rho + \bm{M}\bm{r} \, .$$

Since  $M \in \mathcal{M}_{t,r}$  has columns spanning  $\mathbb{F}^t$ , the linear map  $r \mapsto Mr$  is surjective onto  $\mathbb{F}^t$ . Therefore, when r is uniform in  $\mathbb{F}^r$ , the value Mr is uniform in  $\mathbb{F}^t$ , and hence  $y = t_\rho + Mr$  is uniform in  $\mathbb{F}^t$ , even conditioned on  $(\rho, M)$ . Thus the joint distribution of  $((\rho, M), y)$  is identical to the distribution produced by the simulator.

**Zero-evader error.** Let  $\mathbf{v} \neq 0$  and write  $\mathbf{v} = (\mathbf{s}, \mathbf{r})^{\mathsf{T}}$  for  $\mathbf{s} \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$  and  $\mathbf{r} \in \mathbb{F}^{r}$ . Note that  $\mathsf{ze}'(\rho, \mathbf{M}) \cdot \mathbf{v} = \mathsf{ze}(\rho) \cdot \mathbf{s} + \mathbf{M} \cdot \mathbf{r}$ . We consider two cases.

• If r = 0 then  $s \neq 0$  and then

$$\Pr[\mathsf{ze}'(\rho, \boldsymbol{M}) \cdot \boldsymbol{v} = \boldsymbol{0}] = \Pr[\mathsf{ze}(\rho) \cdot \boldsymbol{s} = \boldsymbol{0}] \leq \varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$$
 .

• If  $r \neq 0$ , write  $t_{\rho} = \text{ze}(\rho) \cdot s$ , in which case

$$\Pr[\mathsf{ze}'(\rho, \boldsymbol{M}) \cdot \boldsymbol{v} = \boldsymbol{0}] = \Pr[\boldsymbol{M} \cdot \boldsymbol{r} = \boldsymbol{t}_\rho]$$
 .

Since  $r \neq 0$ , there exists an invertible matrix  $R \in \mathbb{F}^{r \times r}$  such that  $R \cdot r = e_1$ . Right-multiplication by R preserves the property that the columns span  $\mathbb{F}^t$ , hence the map  $M \mapsto MR$  is a bijection on  $\mathcal{M}_{t,r}$  and therefore

$$\Pr[\boldsymbol{M}\boldsymbol{r}=\boldsymbol{t}_\rho]=\Pr[\boldsymbol{M}\boldsymbol{e}_1=\boldsymbol{t}_\rho]$$
 .

Denote by  $m_1$  the first column of M, so  $Me_1 = m_1$ . We upper bound  $\Pr[m_1 = t_\rho]$ .

If  $t_{\rho} \neq \mathbf{0}$ , then for every  $u \in \mathbb{F}^t \setminus \{\mathbf{0}\}$  the probability  $\Pr[\boldsymbol{m}_1 = \boldsymbol{u}]$  is the same by left-invariance: for any invertible  $\boldsymbol{L} \in \mathbb{F}^{t \times t}$ , the map  $\boldsymbol{M} \mapsto \boldsymbol{L} \boldsymbol{M}$  is a bijection on  $\mathcal{M}_{t,r}$  and sends  $\boldsymbol{m}_1$  to  $\boldsymbol{L} \cdot \boldsymbol{m}_1$ . Hence  $\Pr[\boldsymbol{m}_1 = \boldsymbol{u}]$  is constant over all nonzero  $\boldsymbol{u}$ , and therefore

$$\Pr[\boldsymbol{m}_1 = \boldsymbol{t}_\rho] \leq \frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|^t - 1}$$
 .

If  $t_{\rho} = 0$ , then

$$\Pr_{\boldsymbol{M} \leftarrow \mathcal{M}_{t,r}}[\boldsymbol{m}_1 = \boldsymbol{0}] = \frac{|\mathcal{M}_{t,r-1}|}{|\mathcal{M}_{t,r}|} = \prod_{i=0}^{t-1} \frac{|\mathbb{F}|^{r-1} - |\mathbb{F}|^i}{|\mathbb{F}|^r - |\mathbb{F}|^i} \le |\mathbb{F}|^{-t},$$

where the equality follows by observing that fixing  $m_1 = \mathbf{0}$  leaves a uniformly random matrix in  $\mathbb{F}^{t \times (r-1)}$  whose columns span  $\mathbb{F}^t$ , and the inequality holds since for all i,  $\frac{|\mathbb{F}|^{r-1} - |\mathbb{F}|^i}{|\mathbb{F}|^r - |\mathbb{F}|^i} \leq \frac{|\mathbb{F}|^{r-1}}{|\mathbb{F}|^r} = |\mathbb{F}|^{-1}$ .

Combining the two subcases, for all  $\boldsymbol{t}_{\rho} \in \mathbb{F}^{t}$  we obtain

$$\Pr_{\boldsymbol{M} \leftarrow \mathcal{M}_{t,r}}[\boldsymbol{Mr} = \boldsymbol{t}_{\rho}] \leq \max\left\{\frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|^{t} - 1}, |\mathbb{F}|^{-t}\right\} = \frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|^{t} - 1},$$

and hence, for  $r \neq 0$ ,

$$\Pr[\mathsf{ze}'(\rho, \boldsymbol{M}) \cdot \boldsymbol{v} = \boldsymbol{0}] \leq \frac{1}{|\mathbb{F}|^t - 1} \,.$$

{52}------------------------------------------------

#### <span id="page-52-0"></span>Code-switching complexity 9.3

We define succinct linear forms induced by the generating matrices of (the encoding map of) the code. The complexity of computing such succinct linear forms will directly impact the prover and verifier time of the code-switch protocol that we design.

**Definition 9.4.** Let  $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \Sigma^m \equiv (\mathbb{F}^i)^m$  be an  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^{r} \to \Sigma^{m} \ and \ generating \ matrix \ \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}} = \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#} & \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$} \end{bmatrix}$ . We define two linear forms:

- sl<sup>#</sup> takes as input a state x ∈ [m · ι] and outputs G<sup>#</sup><sub>C</sub>[x, ·] ∈ F<sup>ℓ</sup> (G<sup>#</sup><sub>C</sub> 's x-th row);
  sl<sup>\$\\$</sup> takes as input a state x ∈ [m · ι] and outputs G<sup>\$\\$</sup><sub>C</sub>[x, ·] ∈ F<sup>r</sup> (G<sup>\$\\$</sup><sub>C</sub> 's x-th row). (A minor abuse of notation for simplicity:  $\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}$ ,  $\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}$  actually depend on  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  rather than  $\mathcal{C}$ .)

In our protocols the prover time will depend on  $t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#}$  and  $t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\$}$ , and the verifier time will depend on  $t_{\odot_k(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#)}$  and  $t_{\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\$}$  for some  $k \in \mathbb{N}$ .

For some linear codes such as Reed–Solomon codes over explicit domains, the prover costs can be linear  $O(\ell + \log m + r)$  while the verifier costs can be logarithmic  $O(\log m + r)$  (this fact is implicit in [ACFY25; NA25] and explicit in [BFRW25]).

**Lemma 9.5.** Let  $\mathcal{C} := \mathsf{RS}[\mathbb{F}, \mathcal{L}, \ell + r]$  be a Reed-Solomon code with  $|\mathcal{L}| = m$  and such that there exists a bijection  $\varphi \colon [m] \to \mathcal{L}$  computable in  $O(\log m)$  field operations.<sup>2</sup> There exists a r-query perfect zero-knowledge encoding for C such that: (i) if  $\ell$  is a power-of-two, for every  $i \in [\log \ell]$ ,  $t_{\odot_i(\mathrm{sl}_{\mathcal{L}}^\#)} = O(\ell/2^i + i + \log m); \ (ii) \ t_{\mathrm{sl}_{\mathcal{L}}^\$} = O(r + \log m).$ 

*Proof.* Consider the encoding map  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^{r} \to \mathcal{C}$  that takes as input (f, r), interprets them as coefficients of polynomials  $\hat{f}$ ,  $\hat{r}$  and outputs  $(\hat{f} + X^{\ell} \cdot \hat{r})(\mathcal{L})$ . From prior work (e.g. [BCL22]),  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  is a r-query perfect zero-knowledge encoding for  $\mathcal{C}$ . The encoding matrix of  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  is  $G_{\mathcal{C}} = \mathsf{Inc}_{\mathcal{C}}$  $[\boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}] = [\varphi(x)^{j-1}]_{x \in [m], j \in [\ell+r]}.$ 

Assume that  $\ell$  is a power of two,  $x \in [m]$ ,  $\gamma \in \mathbb{F}^i$ , and consider  $\bigcirc_i \mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#(x, \gamma)$ . By definition, for every  $c \in \{0, 1\}^{\log \ell - i}$ ,

$$\begin{split} (\odot_i \mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#(x, \pmb{\gamma}))[\pmb{c}] &= \sum_{\pmb{b} \in \{0, 1\}^i} \mathsf{eq}(\pmb{b}, \pmb{\gamma}) \cdot \pmb{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#[x, \pmb{b}, \pmb{c}] \\ &= \sum_{\pmb{b} \in \{0, 1\}^i} \mathsf{eq}(\pmb{b}, \pmb{\gamma}) \cdot \varphi(x)^{\sum_{t \in [i]} b_t \cdot 2^{t-1} + \sum_{t \in [\log \ell - i]} c_t \cdot 2^{i+t-1}} \\ &= \sum_{\pmb{b} \in \{0, 1\}^i} \mathsf{eq}(\pmb{b}, \pmb{\gamma}) \cdot \prod_{t \in [i]} \varphi(x)^{b_t \cdot 2^{t-1}} \cdot \prod_{t \in [\log \ell - i]} \varphi(x)^{c_t \cdot 2^{i+t-1}} \\ &= \left(\prod_{t \in [\log \ell - i]} \varphi(x)^{c_t \cdot 2^{i+t-1}}\right) \cdot \left(\sum_{\pmb{b} \in \{0, 1\}^i} \mathsf{eq}(\pmb{b}, \pmb{\gamma}) \cdot \prod_{t \in [i]} ((1 - b_t) \cdot 1 + b_t \cdot \varphi(x)^{2^{t-1}})\right) \\ &= \left(\prod_{t \in [\log \ell - i]} \varphi(x)^{c_t \cdot 2^{i+t-1}}\right) \cdot \prod_{t \in [i]} (1 - \gamma_t + \gamma_t \cdot \varphi(x)^{2^{t-1}}) \,. \end{split}$$

Where we have used the fact that one of the quantities was multilinear in b and  $\sum_{b} eq(b, \gamma) \cdot \hat{p}(b) =$  $\hat{p}(\gamma)$  for any multilinear polynomial  $\hat{p}$ . This yields an algorithm to compute  $\odot_i \mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^\#(x,\gamma)$ :

<sup>&</sup>lt;sup>2</sup>This class includes many commonly used Reed-Solomon codes over finite field, but excludes (for example) Reed-Solomon codes where  $\mathcal{L}$  is a random subset of the field.

{53}------------------------------------------------

- 1. Compute  $\varphi(x)$  in  $O(\log m)$  field operations.
- 2. Compute  $\prod_{t \in [i]} (1 \gamma_t + \gamma_t \cdot \varphi(x)^{2^{t-1}})$  in O(i) field operations.
- 3. Compute  $\left(\prod_{t\in[\log\ell-i]}^{c_t}\varphi(x)^{c_t\cdot 2^{i+t-1}}\right)_{c\in\{0,1\}^{\log\ell-i}}$  in  $O(\ell/2^i)$  field operations using a dynamic programming algorithm (e.g., [VSBW13; BCFFMMZ25]).
- 4. Compute the final expression in  $O(\ell/2^i)$  field operations.

To conclude the lemma, one can see that for every  $x \in [m], G_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x,\cdot] = [\varphi(x)^{\ell+i-1}]_{j \in [r]}$  can be computed in  $O(\log m + r)$  field operations. 

#### <span id="page-53-0"></span>Code-switching IOR 9.4

<span id="page-53-1"></span>We describe an IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}',\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$ .

#### Theorem 9.6. Let:

- $n \in \mathbb{N}$  be a number of functions.
- $t, t_{\text{ood}} \in \mathbb{N}$  be repetition parameters.
