- $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \Sigma^m \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota})^m$  be an  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with zero-knowledge encoding  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ .  $\mathcal{C}' \subseteq (\Sigma')^{m'} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota'})^{m'}$  be a  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^{r'_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \mathbb{F}^{r'_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  $(\Sigma')^{m'}$ .
- $C_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  be a  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}}$
- $\mathbf{sl} = (\mathbf{sl}, (\mathbf{sl}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$  where  $\mathbf{sl} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathbf{zk}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathbf{zk}}}|.$   $Let \ \mathbf{ze} \colon D_{\mathbf{ze}} \to \mathbb{F}^{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+t \cdot \iota}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$  and let  $\mathbf{ze}_{\leftrightarrow} \colon D_{\mathsf{ze}} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{\mathsf{ood}}}$  denote the first  $t_{ood}$  coefficients of ze (skipping the first one).
- Let  $ze_{ood}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times (\ell + \ell_{zk})}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{ood}$ . Write  $ze_{ood} = (ze_{ood}^{\leftarrow}, ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow})$  where  $ze_{ood}^{\leftarrow}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times \ell}$  and  $ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times \ell_{zk}}$  denote the first and last components of  $ze_{ood}$ . For every  $i \in [t_{\text{ood}}]$  denote by  $\mathsf{ze}_{\text{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i}$  (resp.  $\mathsf{ze}_{\text{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}$ ) the zero-evader obtained by restricting  $\mathsf{ze}_{\text{ood}}^{\leftarrow}$  (resp.  $ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow}$ ) to the i-th row.

Define

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{sl}' &\coloneqq \mathbf{ze}[\times(\mathbf{sl}), (\mathbf{ze}_{\mathtt{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i})_{i \in [t_{\mathtt{ood}}]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#})_{i \in [t], l \in [\iota]}] \\ \mathbf{sl}'_{n+1} &\coloneqq \mathbf{ze}_{\leftrightarrow}[(\mathbf{sl}_{\mathtt{ze}_{\mathtt{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}})_{i \in [t_{\mathtt{ood}}]}, (0^{\ell_{\mathtt{zk}} - r}(\mathbf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}))_{i \in [t], l \in [\iota]}] \\ \mathbf{sl}' &\coloneqq \left(\mathbf{sl}', (\times(\mathbf{sl}_i))_{i \in [n]}, \mathbf{sl}'_{n+1}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}, \mathbf{sl}_{\mathtt{id}}\right). \end{split}$$

Construction 9.7 is an IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}',\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$  with the following properties.

- Round complexity: 2.
- Prover communication (in field elements):  $m' \cdot \iota' + m_{zk} \cdot \iota_{zk} + \iota_{ood}$ . Of these,
  - $-m' \cdot \iota'$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma'$ ,
  - $-m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}$ , and
  - $t_{\text{ood}}$  are sent as a non-oracle message.
- Query complexity: t queries to the first input oracle.
- Prover time (in field operations):  $O(\mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}') + \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}) + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}) + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i}).$
- Verifier time (in field operations):  $O(\text{teval}(ze) + t_{ood})$ .

{54}------------------------------------------------

• Round-by-round security: For every  $\delta, \delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0, 1)$ , Construction 9.7 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $(\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}^{\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}, \tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}', \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}'}^{\delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}})$  and errors

$$\left(\frac{(|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|)^2}{2}\cdot\varepsilon_{\mathsf{ood}},\ (1-\delta)^t,\ |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+1}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|\cdot\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}\right).$$

The total extraction time is O(tenc(C)).

• **Zero-knowledge:** If  $ze_{ood}$  is a  $(\ell_{zk}-r, \zeta_{ze})$ -private zero-evader, C' has a t'-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{C'}$ , and  $C_{zk}$  has a  $t_{zk}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{C_{zk}}$ , then, for every  $t \in \mathbb{N}^n$ , Construction 9.7 is HVZK for  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t',t,t_{zk})}$  with error  $\zeta_{C'} + \zeta_{ze} + \zeta_{C_{zk}}$  and query complexity (t,t).

#### <span id="page-54-0"></span>Construction 9.7.

- Inputs. The verifier receives explicit input  $\mathbb{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), ((\boldsymbol{\mu}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}))$  and oracle access to implicit input  $\mathbb{y} = (f, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . In the honest case, the prover receives as input  $\mathbb{x}$  and  $\mathbb{y}$  as well as witness  $\mathbb{w} = (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  such that  $(\mathbb{x}, \mathbb{y}, \mathbb{w}) \in \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}$ .
- Interaction phase.
  - 1. **Send witness.** The prover sends  $g \in (\Sigma')^{m'}$  and  $s \in \Sigma_{zk}^{m_{zk}}$ . In the honest case, the prover samples  $\mathbf{r}' \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r'}$ ,  $\mathbf{s} \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{zk}-r}$ ,  $\mathbf{r}'' \leftarrow \mathbb{F}^{r_{zk}}$  and computes  $g \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}(\mathbf{f}, \mathbf{r}')$  and  $s \coloneqq \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{zk}}((\mathbf{r}, \mathbf{s}), \mathbf{r}'')$ .
  - 2. Out-of-domain samples. The verifier samples and sends  $\rho_{\text{ood}} \leftarrow D_{\text{ood}}$ .
  - 3. Out-of-domain answers. The prover sends  $y \in \mathbb{F}^{t_{\text{ood}}}$ . In the honest case the prover computes

<span id="page-54-1"></span>
$$\boldsymbol{y}\coloneqq \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}})\cdot \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{f} \ \boldsymbol{r} \ \boldsymbol{s} \end{bmatrix}$$
 .

- 4. In-domain queries and batching. The verifier samples and sends  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$  and  $\rho \leftarrow D_{ze}$ . Set  $\boldsymbol{\nu} \coloneqq \mathsf{ze}(\rho)$  and for  $i \in [t]$ , let  $\boldsymbol{x}_i \coloneqq \mathsf{binary}(x_i)$ .
- **Decision phase.** The verifier queries  $f(x_1), \ldots, f(x_t) \in \Sigma$ , and computes

$$\mu' \coloneqq \boldsymbol{\nu}_1 \cdot \mu + \sum_{i \in [t_{\text{ood}}]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+i} \cdot y_i + \sum_{i \in [t]} \sum_{l \in [\iota]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+t_{\text{ood}}+i\cdot\iota+l} \cdot f(x_i)_l.$$

The verifier further sets  $\mathsf{st}' \coloneqq \mathsf{st}'_{n+1} \coloneqq (\rho, \mathsf{st}, (\rho_{\mathsf{ood}})_{i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]}, (x_{1,l}, \dots, x_{t,l})_{l \in [\iota]})$ , where  $x_{j,l} \coloneqq \iota \cdot x_j + l$ . The verifier outputs the following new explicit instance and implicit instance and in the honest case the prover outputs the following new witness:

$$\mathbf{z}' \coloneqq ((\boldsymbol{\mu}', \mathsf{st}', (\boldsymbol{\nu}_1, \mathsf{st}_1), \dots, (\boldsymbol{\nu}_1, \mathsf{st}_n), \mathsf{sl}'_{n+1}), ((\boldsymbol{\mu}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{st}_{\circ, i})_{i \in [n]}), (0, 0^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}})), 
\mathbf{y}' \coloneqq (g, (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i)_{i \in [n]}, s), 
\mathbf{w}' \coloneqq ((\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}'), (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, ((\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}), \boldsymbol{r}'')).$$
(9)

{55}------------------------------------------------

Completeness. We show that the construction is perfectly complete. In an honest execution

$$\begin{split} \mu &= \langle \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \\ \forall i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]: \ y_i &= \langle (\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}), \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}})[i] \rangle = \langle \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) \rangle + \langle (\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}), \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) \rangle \\ \forall i \in [t], \ \forall \, l \in [\iota]: \ f(x_i)_l &= \langle \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle + \langle \boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle \\ &= \langle \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle + \langle (\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}), (\boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot], \boldsymbol{0}) \rangle \,. \end{split}$$

By linearity then,

$$\begin{aligned} \mu' &= \left\langle \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{\nu}_1 \cdot \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) + \sum_{i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+i} \cdot \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) + \sum_{i \in [t]} \sum_{l \in [t]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+i \cdot \iota + l} \cdot \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \right\rangle \\ &+ \sum_{i \in [n]} \left\langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\nu}_1 \cdot \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \right\rangle \\ &+ \left\langle (\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}), \sum_{i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+i} \cdot \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) + \sum_{i \in [t]} \sum_{l \in [\iota]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+i \cdot \iota + l} \cdot \left\langle \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot], \boldsymbol{0} \right) \right\rangle . \end{aligned}$$

### <span id="page-55-0"></span>9.5 Zero-knowledge

**Lemma 9.8.** If  $ze_{ood}$  is a  $(\ell_{zk}-r, \zeta_{ze})$ -private zero-evader, C' has a t'-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{C'}$ , and  $C_{zk}$  has a  $t_{zk}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{C_{zk}}$ , then, for every  $t \in \mathbb{N}^n$ , Construction 9.7 is HVZK for  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t',t,t_{zk})}$  with error  $\zeta_{C'} + \zeta_{ze} + \zeta_{C_{zk}}$  and query complexity (t,t).

*Proof.* We describe the simulator S for Construction 9.7.

$$\mathbf{S}^{y,\mathcal{D}}(\mathbf{x})$$
:

- 1. Parse y as  $y = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ .
- 2. Sample  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$  and  $\rho \leftarrow D_{ze}$ .
- 3. Sample  $(\rho_{ood}, \boldsymbol{y}) \leftarrow \mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{ze}_{ood}}$ .
- 4. Query  $f(x_1), \ldots, f(x_t)$  and derive  $\mathbb{Z}'$  as in Equation 9.
- 5. Run  $\mathcal{D}$  on  $\mathbf{z}'$ , answering queries to  $\mathbf{y}'$  as follows:
  - When  $\mathcal{D}$  queries one of  $(\xi_i)_{i\in[n]}$ , query the corresponding oracle accordingly (denote these answers as  $Q_{\xi}$ ).
  - When  $\mathcal{D}$  queries g, answer according to  $\mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}'}$  (denote these answers as  $Q_g$ ).
  - When  $\mathcal{D}$  queries s, answer according to  $\mathsf{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  (denote these answers as  $Q_s$ ).
- 6. Let out denote  $\mathcal{D}$ 's output.
- 7. Output  $(\rho, (x_1, \ldots, x_t), (f(x_1), \ldots, f(x_t)), Q_{\xi}, Q_g, Q_s, y, \text{out}).$

The proof follows by a sequence of hybrids  $H_0, \ldots, H_3$ . The first hybrid  $H_0$  is the real experiment. In the second hybrid  $H_1$ , the distribution of  $(\rho_{\text{ood}}, \boldsymbol{y})$  is replaced to be sampled by  $S_{\text{ze}_{\text{ood}}}$ ; the statistical distance between  $H_0$  and  $H_1$  is then bounded by  $\zeta_{\text{ze}}$ . In the third hybrid  $H_2$ , the queries to g are replaced by answers according to  $\text{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}'}$ ; the statistical distance between  $H_1$  and  $H_2$  is then bounded by  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}'}$ . In the fourth hybrid  $H_3$ , the queries to s are replaced by answers according to  $\text{Sim}_{\mathcal{C}_{\text{zk}}}$ , and thus the experiment is simulated experiment; the statistical distance between  $H_2$  and  $H_3$  is then bounded by  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\text{zk}}}$ .

{56}------------------------------------------------

## <span id="page-56-0"></span>9.6 Round-by-round knowledge soundness

<span id="page-56-1"></span>**Lemma 9.9.** For every  $\delta, \delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0, 1)$ , Construction 9.7 has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $(\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}^{\delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}, \tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}', \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}'}^{\delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}})$  and errors

$$\left(\frac{(|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|)^2}{2}\cdot\varepsilon_{\mathsf{ood}},\ (1-\delta)^t,\ |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv n+1}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|\cdot\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}\right).$$

The total extraction time is O(tenc(C)).

*Proof.* We give notation, describe the extractors, describe a state function, and finally we establish the RBR knowledge soundness errors (based on the extractor and state function).

**Notation.** Let  $\mathbf{x} = ((\mu, \mathsf{st}_0, (\mathsf{st}_i)_{i \in [n]}), (\boldsymbol{\mu}_i, \mathsf{st}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]})$  and  $\mathbf{y} = (f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$ . A complete transcript of the protocol has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = ((g, s), \rho_{\mathsf{ood}}, \boldsymbol{y}, (x_1, \dots, x_t, \rho))$ .

**Extractors.** We describe the round-by-round extractors from the last round to the first.

- 1. **Final round.**  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || (x_1, \dots, x_t, \rho), \mathsf{w})$  outputs the witness  $\mathsf{w}$ .
- 2. Out-of-domain samples.  $\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathbf{x}, \mathbf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || \rho_{\mathsf{ood}}, \mathsf{w})$ :
  - (a) Parse w as  $((\bar{g}, \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}'), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}, \boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}''))$ .
  - (b) Parse  $\boldsymbol{s}$  as  $(\boldsymbol{r}, \boldsymbol{s}') \in \mathbb{F}^r \times \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} r}$ .
  - (c) Compute  $\bar{f} := \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g, r)$ .
  - (d) Output  $((\bar{f}, \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}).$
- 3. Initial round.
  - (a) Parse w as  $((\bar{f}, \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$ .
  - (b) Set  $\mathbb{w} \coloneqq ((\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), (\boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}).$
  - (c) Set  $y^* := (\bar{f}, (\bar{\xi}_i)_{i \in [n]}).$
  - (d) Output  $(w, y^*)$ .

The state function. We define a state function KState.

0. **Initial transcript:** We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\emptyset,\mathsf{w})=1$  if and only if  $(\mathtt{x},\mathtt{y},\mathsf{w})\in \tilde{\mathcal{R}}^{\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}},$  that is

$$\mathsf{w} = \left((\bar{f}, \boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}\right)$$

is such that:

- $\Delta((f,\xi_1,\ldots,\xi_n),(\bar{f},\bar{\xi}_1,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n)) \leq (\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}},\ldots,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
- $\bar{f} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), \, \forall \, i \in [n] \, \bar{\xi_i} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\operatorname{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i});$
- $\forall i \in [n] \operatorname{sl}_{\circ,i}(\operatorname{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
- $\langle \boldsymbol{f}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu.$
- 1. Out-of-domain samples: The transcript has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = ((g, s))$ . The verifier samples  $\rho_{\mathsf{ood}} \leftarrow D_{\mathsf{ood}}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} \| \rho_{\mathsf{ood}}, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if either of the following hold:

{57}------------------------------------------------

- <span id="page-57-0"></span>(a)  $\mathbf{w} = ((\bar{f}, \mathbf{f}, \mathbf{r}), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]})$  is such that:
  - $\Delta((f,\xi_1,\ldots,\xi_n),(\bar{f},\bar{\xi}_1,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n)) \leq (\delta,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}},\ldots,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
  - $\bar{f} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(\boldsymbol{f}, \boldsymbol{r}), \, \forall \, i \in [n] \, \bar{\xi_i} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{7k}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i});$
  - $\forall i \in [n] \operatorname{sl}_{\circ,i}(\operatorname{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
  - $\langle f, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \xi_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu.$
- <span id="page-57-1"></span>(b) there exist distinct  $(\boldsymbol{g}_0, \boldsymbol{s}_0) \neq (\boldsymbol{g}_1, \boldsymbol{s}_1)$  and  $(\boldsymbol{r}_0', \boldsymbol{r}_0'', \boldsymbol{r}_1', \boldsymbol{r}_1'')$  such that  $\Delta(g, \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}(\boldsymbol{g}_0, \boldsymbol{r}_0')) \leq \delta'$  and  $\Delta(s, \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s}_0, \boldsymbol{r}_0'')) \leq \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}$ ,  $\Delta(g, \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}(\boldsymbol{g}_1, \boldsymbol{r}_1')) \leq \delta'$  and  $\Delta(s, \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s}_1, \boldsymbol{r}_1'')) \leq \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}$  and

$$\mathsf{ze}_\mathsf{ood}(\rho_\mathsf{ood}) \cdot \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{g}_0 \ \boldsymbol{s}_0 \end{bmatrix} = \mathsf{ze}_\mathsf{ood}(\rho_\mathsf{ood}) \cdot \begin{bmatrix} \boldsymbol{g}_1 \ \boldsymbol{s}_1 \end{bmatrix} \,.$$

2. **In-domain samples:** The transcript has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = ((g, s), \rho_{\mathsf{ood}}, \boldsymbol{y})$ . The verifier samples  $x_1, \ldots, x_t \leftarrow [m]$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} || (x_1, \ldots, x_t), \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if

$$\mathsf{w} = \left((\bar{g}, \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}'), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}, \boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}'')\right)$$

is such that:

- $\Delta((g,\xi_1,\ldots,\xi_n,s),(\bar{g},\bar{\xi}_1,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n,\bar{s})) \leq (\delta',\delta_{\mathsf{zk}},\ldots,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
- $\bar{g} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}(\boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}'), \, \forall \, i \in [n] \, \bar{\xi_i} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{Tk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i}), \, \bar{s} = \mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{Tk}}}(\boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}'');$
- $g, \operatorname{sl}(\operatorname{st})\rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \xi_i, \operatorname{sl}_i(\operatorname{st}_i) \rangle = \mu;$
- $\forall i \in [n], \, \mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
- $\forall i \in [t_{\text{ood}}], \langle (\boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{s}), \text{ze}_{\text{ood}}(\rho_{\text{ood}})[i] \rangle = y_i;$
- $\forall i \in [t], l \in [\iota], \langle \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle + \langle \boldsymbol{s}, (\boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot], \boldsymbol{0}) \rangle = f(x_i)_l$
- 3. Combination randomness: The transcript has the form  $\mathsf{tr} = ((g, s), \rho_{\mathsf{ood}}, \boldsymbol{y}, (x_1, \dots, x_t))$ . The verifier samples  $\rho \leftarrow D_{\mathsf{ze}}$ . We set  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr} \| \rho, \mathsf{w}) = 1$  if and only if

$$\mathsf{w} = \left((\bar{g}, \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}'), (\bar{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \boldsymbol{r}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\bar{s}, \boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}'')\right)$$

is such that:

- $\Delta((g,\xi_1,\ldots,\xi_n,s),(\bar{g},\bar{\xi}_1,\ldots,\bar{\xi}_n,\bar{s})) \leq (\delta',\delta_{\mathsf{zk}},\ldots,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}});$
- $\bar{g} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}(\boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}'), \, \forall \, i \in [n] \, \bar{\xi_i} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{\xi_i}, \boldsymbol{r_i}), \, \bar{s} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}(\boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}'');$
- $\forall i \in [n] \operatorname{sl}_{\circ,i}(\operatorname{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i;$
- the following holds

$$\begin{split} \mu' &= \left\langle \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{\nu}_1 \cdot \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) + \sum_{i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+i} \cdot \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) + \sum_{i \in [t]} \sum_{l \in [\iota]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+i \cdot \iota + l} \cdot \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \right\rangle \\ &+ \boldsymbol{\nu}_1 \cdot \sum_{i \in [n]} \left\langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \right\rangle \\ &+ \left\langle \boldsymbol{s}, \sum_{i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+i} \cdot \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}}) + \sum_{i \in [t]} \sum_{l \in [\iota]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+i \cdot \iota + l} \cdot \left( \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot], \boldsymbol{0} \right) \right\rangle. \end{split}$$

{58}------------------------------------------------

Bounding the errors. We bound the RBR errors for the protocol.

#### 1. Out-of-domain samples. We show that

$$\Pr\left[\exists\,\mathsf{w}:\begin{array}{l}\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w})) = 0\\ \land\,\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|\rho_{\mathsf{ood}},\mathsf{w}) = 1\end{array}\right] \leq \frac{(|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|)^2}{2}\cdot\varepsilon_{\mathsf{ood}}\,.$$

Note that Item 1a is independent of  $\rho_{ood}$ , and so it cannot hold. It must then be that Item 1b holds, but the probability of this holding is bound by Lemma 9.1.

# 2. In-domain samples. We show that

$$\Pr\left[\exists\,\mathsf{w}:\ \, \frac{\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w}))=0}{\land\,\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|(x_1,\ldots,x_t),\mathsf{w})=1}\,\right]\leq (1-\delta)^t\,.$$

Fix w such that  $\mathsf{KState}(x, y, \mathsf{tr} | (x_1, \dots, x_t), \mathsf{w}) = 1$  and  $\mathsf{KState}(x, y, \mathsf{tr}, \mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(x, y, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w})) = 0$ . Then, it must be that for  $i \in [n]$  we have that  $\mathsf{sl}_{\circ,i}(\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}) \cdot \boldsymbol{\xi}_i = \boldsymbol{\mu}_i$  and this must also hold in Item 1a.

Note that  $\Delta((g,s),(\bar{g},\bar{s})) \leq (\delta',\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})$ , and so by Item 1b there must be a unique choice of (g,s) in w such that for every  $i \in [t_{\mathsf{ood}}]$  it holds that  $\langle (g,s), \mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood}}(\rho_{\mathsf{ood}})[i] \rangle = y_i$  (note also that every condition involving  $x_1, \ldots, x_t$  only depends on the (g,s) portion of the witness).

Now, suppose that for this  $(\boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{r}', \boldsymbol{s}, \boldsymbol{r}^*)$  it held that

$$\langle \boldsymbol{g}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle = \mu \,,$$

and parse  $s = (r^*, s')$ . Let  $\bar{f} = \operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}}(g, r^*)$ . It must be that  $\Delta(f, \bar{f}) > \delta$ , as else it contradicts the assumption  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x}, \mathsf{y}, \mathsf{tr}, \mathsf{w})) = 0$ . But then, the probability that for every  $i \in [t], l \in [\iota]$  it holds that  $f(x_i)_l = \bar{f}(x_i)_l = \langle g, G_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle + \langle r^*, G_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle$  is at most  $(1 - \delta)^t$ .

# 3. Combination randomness. We show that

$$\Pr\left[\exists\,\mathsf{w}:\begin{array}{l}\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w}))=0\\ \land\,\mathsf{KState}(\mathsf{x},\mathsf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|\rho,\mathsf{w})=1\end{array}\right] \leq |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n+1},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|\cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}\,.$$

Fix w such that  $\mathsf{KState}(x,y,\mathsf{tr},\mathbf{E}_{\mathsf{rbr}}(x,y,\mathsf{tr},\mathsf{w})) = 0$ . Then, it must be that at least one of the three conditions are not satisfied, namely either:

$$\langle \boldsymbol{g}, \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}) \rangle + \sum_{i \in [n]} \langle \boldsymbol{\xi}_i, \mathsf{sl}_i(\mathsf{st}_i) \rangle \neq \mu,$$

- or for some  $i \in [t_{ood}]$  it holds that  $\langle (\boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{s}), \mathsf{ze}_{ood}(\rho_{ood})[i] \rangle \neq y_i$ .
- or for some  $i \in [t], l \in [\iota]$  it holds that  $\langle \boldsymbol{g}, \boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#}[x_{i,l}, \cdot] \rangle + \langle \boldsymbol{s}, (\boldsymbol{G}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}[x_{i,l}, \cdot], \boldsymbol{0}) \rangle \neq f(x_i)_l$ .

Then, the probability that  $\mathsf{KState}(\mathbf{z},\mathbf{y},\mathsf{tr}\|\rho,\mathsf{w})=1$  is at most  $\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$ . Taking a union bound over the  $|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}',\delta')|\cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n+1},\delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|$  possible choices of  $\mathsf{w}$  concludes the proof.

{59}------------------------------------------------

## <span id="page-59-0"></span>9.7 Proof of Theorem 2

We combine Construction 6.3 and Construction 9.7 to give a formal statement and proof of Theorem 2.

#### <span id="page-59-1"></span>Theorem 9.10. Let:

- $n \in \mathbb{N}$ ;
- $k, t, t_{\text{ood}} \in \mathbb{N}$ ;
- $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \Sigma^m \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota})^m$  be an  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell} \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ ;
- $C_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  be a  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{C_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon$
- $\mathcal{C}' \subseteq (\Sigma')^{m'} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota'})^{m'}$  be a  $\mathbb{F}$ -additive code with zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'} \colon \mathbb{F}^\ell \times \mathbb{F}^{r'_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to (\Sigma')^{m'};$
- $\bullet \ \mathbf{sI} = (\mathsf{sI}, (\mathsf{sI}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathsf{sI}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}) \ where \ \mathsf{sI} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^\ell |, \ \mathsf{sI}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{Zk}}} |, \ \mathsf{sI}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathsf{Zk}}} |;$
- ze:  $D_{ze} \to \mathbb{F}^{1+t_{\mathsf{ood}}+t\cdot t}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}}$ , and let  $\mathsf{ze}_{\leftrightarrow} \colon D_{\mathsf{ze}} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{\mathsf{ood}}}$  denote the first  $t_{\mathsf{ood}}$  coefficients of  $\mathsf{ze}$  (skipping the first one);
- $ze_{ood}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times (\ell + \ell_{zk})}$  be a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{ood}$ , and write  $ze_{ood} = (ze_{ood}^{\leftarrow}, ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow})$  with  $ze_{ood}^{\leftarrow}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times \ell}$  and  $ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow}: D_{ood} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{ood} \times \ell_{zk}}$ . For  $i \in [t_{ood}]$ , denote by  $ze_{ood}^{\leftarrow,i}$  and  $ze_{ood}^{\rightarrow,i}$  the corresponding row-restricted zero-evaders.

Define

$$\begin{split} \mathbf{sl'} &\coloneqq \mathbf{ze}[\times(\odot_k\mathbf{sl}), (\mathbf{ze}_{\mathrm{ood}}^{\leftarrow,i})_{i\in[t_{\mathrm{ood}}]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\#})_{i\in[t],l\in[\iota]}] \,, \\ \mathbf{sl'}_{n+k+1} &\coloneqq \mathbf{ze}_{\leftrightarrow}[(\mathbf{sl}_{\mathbf{ze}_{\mathrm{ood}}^{\rightarrow,i}})_{i\in[t_{\mathrm{ood}}]}, (0^{\ell_{\mathbf{zk}}-r}(\mathbf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}}^{\$}))_{i\in[t],l\in[\iota]}] \\ \mathbf{sl'} &\coloneqq \left(\mathbf{sl'}, (\times(\mathbf{sl}_i))_{i\in[n]}, (\times(\mathbf{sl}_{\mathbf{ze}_{\ell_{\mathbf{zk}}}^{\star}}))_{j\in[k]}, \mathbf{sl'}_{n+k+1}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i\in[n]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\mathrm{id}})_{j\in[k+1]}\right) \,. \end{split}$$

There exists an IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}',\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$  with the following properties:

- Round complexity: k + 3.
- Prover communication (in field elements):  $k \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}) + 1 + m' \cdot \iota' + m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} + t_{\mathsf{ood}}$ . Of these,  $m' \cdot \iota'$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma'$ ,  $(k+1) \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}$  are sent as an oracle over  $\Sigma^{k+1}$  and  $k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + t_{\mathsf{ood}} + 1$  are sent as non-oracle messages.
- Query complexity: t queries to the first input oracle.
- Prover time (in field operations):  $O(\ell \cdot 2^k + t_{sl} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{sl_i} + tenc(\mathcal{C}') + k \cdot tenc(\mathcal{C}_{zk}) + teval(ze) + teval(ze_{ood}))$ .
- Verifier time (in field operations):  $O(k \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}))$ .
- Round-by-round security: For  $\delta, \delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0, 1)$ , the protocol has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $(\tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C} \equiv 2^k, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}}^{\delta, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}, \tilde{\mathcal{R}}_{\mathcal{C}', \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}'}^{\delta', \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}})$  with errors

$$\left( \begin{array}{c} \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n+k}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \left( \epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}}, \delta) + \frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-(j-1)}}, \delta)| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n+k}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|} \right)_{j \in [k]}, \\ \frac{(|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}', \delta')| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|)^2}{2} \cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{ood}}, (1 - \delta)^t, |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}', \delta')| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv n+k+1}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})| \cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero}} \end{array} \right)$$

and extraction time  $O\left(\sum_{j\in[k]}\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^{k-j}})+\mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C})\right)$ .

- Zero-knowledge: Suppose that  $char(\mathbb{F}) \neq 2$ ,  $\ell_{zk} \geq 2$ , and:
  - $ze_{ood}$  is a  $(\ell_{zk} r, \zeta_{ze})$ -private zero-evader;

{60}------------------------------------------------

- $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}'}$  is a t'-query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}'}$ ;
- $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  is a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . Then, for every  $\mathbf{t} \in \mathbb{N}^n$ , the protocol is HVZK for  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t', \mathbf{t}, (t_{\mathsf{zk}})_j \in [k+1])}$  with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}'} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze}} + (k+1) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and simulator query complexity  $(t, \mathbf{t})$ .

*Proof.* Let  $\mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{sc}} \colon \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C} \equiv 2^k, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}} \to \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{sc}}}$  be the IOR from Theorem 6.2 and let  $\mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{cs}} \colon \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{sc}}} \to \mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{sc}}}$  be the IOR from Theorem 9.6 (with n + k mask oracles). Define  $\mathsf{IOR} \coloneqq \mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{cs}} \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{sc}}$ .

The round, communication, and time bounds follow by adding the corresponding bounds of the two theorems. The round-by-round knowledge soundness statement (including the error vector and extraction time) follows from Theorem 4.5 together with the two constituent RBR guarantees.

For zero-knowledge, fix any  $\mathcal{D} \in \mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t',t,(t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{j \in [k+1]})}$ , and let  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{cs}}$  be the simulator from the HVZK guarantee of  $\mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{cs}}$ . Set  $\mathcal{D}_* := \mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{cs}}}$ . By the query bounds of  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{cs}}$ ,  $\mathcal{D}_*$  queries (i) f at most t times; (ii) the i-th original mask at most  $t_i$  times for  $i \in [n]$ ; and (iii) each of the k masks introduced by sumcheck at most  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  times. Hence  $\mathcal{D}_*$  is in the query class required by Theorem 6.2. Applying that theorem gives a simulator  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathsf{sc}}$  with error  $k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  and with exactly the claimed query complexity to the original implicit instance.

Apply Theorem 4.5 to  $IOR_{sc}$  and  $IOR_{cs}$ . The composed simulator error is

$$(k \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}) + (\zeta_{\mathcal{C}'} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze}} + \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}) = \zeta_{\mathcal{C}'} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze}} + (k+1) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}.$$

{61}------------------------------------------------

#### <span id="page-61-0"></span>Zero-knowledge IOPP for constrained codes 10

We construct a zero-knowledge IOPP for constrained codes. This yields a formal statement and proof of Theorem 4, and can be seen as a zero-knowledge variant (and generalization) of both WHIR |ACFY25| and Ligerito |NA25|.

**Batched linear forms.** We are going to iteratively use the IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}^{\equiv 2^k},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}',\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}'}$  in Theorem 9.10; in this IOR the prover incurs (among others) the cost  $t_{sl} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{sl_i}$  associated to  $sl = (sl, sl_1, \dots, sl_n)$ . In particular, the second invocation after the first incurs this cost relative to the new linear form sl' (defined in Theorem 9.10). A similar cost is also incurred by the verifier. In both cases, the prover and verifier costs associated to sl' involve batch of linear forms.

**Definition 10.1.** Let  $sl \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t \times n} | \text{ and let } b \in \mathbb{N}$ . We let b(sl, b) denote the number of field operation to compute  $\sum_{i \in [b]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_i \cdot \mathsf{sl}(\mathsf{st}_i) \in \mathbb{F}^{t \times n}$  given  $(\mathsf{st}_1, \dots, \mathsf{st}_b)$  and  $\boldsymbol{\nu} \in \mathbb{F}^b$ . Note that  $\mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}, b) \leq b \cdot t_{\mathsf{sl}} + O(b \cdot t \cdot n)$ .

For many linear forms (e.g., the one in Section 9.3) the cost to compute such batches can be much smaller than  $O(b \cdot t \cdot n)$ . To see this, fix a matrix  $\mathbf{M} \in \mathbb{F}^{m \times \ell}$  and let  $|\mathbf{M}|$  denote the number of field operations to compute  $M \cdot v$  for any  $v \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ . Let  $\mathsf{sl}_M$  be linear form mapping  $x \in [m]$  to  $M[x,\cdot] \in \mathbb{F}^{\ell}$ . We argue that  $b(\mathsf{sl}_{M},b) = O(b+|M|)$ . Fix  $x_1,\ldots,x_b$  and  $\nu$ . Then  $\sum_{i} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{i \in [b]} \cdot \boldsymbol{M}[x_i, \cdot] = \boldsymbol{M}^\mathsf{T} \cdot \left(\sum_{i \in [b]} \boldsymbol{\nu}_{i \in [b]} \cdot \boldsymbol{e}_{x_i}\right)$  where for  $i \in [m]$ , the vector  $\boldsymbol{e}_i \in \mathbb{F}^m$  is the unit vector with 1 in position i and 0 everywhere else. This quantity can be computed in  $O(b + |\mathbf{M}^{\mathsf{T}}|)$ field operations, which is  $O(b + |\mathbf{M}|)$  operations by the transposition principle |Bor57; Ber|.

The main theorem in this section follows by iteratively applying the zero-Main theorem. knowledge sumcheck IOR in Section 6 and the zero-knowledge code-switching IOR in Section 9.

#### **Theorem 10.2.** Fix the following:

- $n \in \mathbb{N}$  and  $\mathfrak{n} \in \mathbb{N}$  with  $\mathfrak{n} \geq 2$ ;
- $\forall i \in [\mathfrak{n}], \ \mathcal{C}_i \subseteq \Sigma_i^{m_i} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_i})^{m_i}$  with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_i} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_i} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_i} \to \Sigma_i^{m_i};$   $\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}} \equiv (\mathbb{F}^{\iota_{\mathsf{zk}}})^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\operatorname{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathsf{zk}}}$  with  $\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \geq$  $\max_{\mathfrak{i}\in[\mathfrak{n}]}r_{\mathfrak{i}};$
- $\mathbf{sl}_0 = (\mathbf{sl}, (\mathbf{sl}_i)_{i \in [n]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i})_{i \in [n]}) \ where \ \mathbf{sl} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_i \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i} \in \langle \mathbb{F}^{t_i \times \ell_{\mathsf{zk}}} |;$
- $\forall i \in [n-1]$ :
  - $-k_{\mathbf{i}}, t_{\mathbf{i}}, t_{\mathsf{ood}, \mathbf{i}} \in \mathbb{N};$
  - $-\operatorname{ze}_{i}:D_{\operatorname{ze},i}\to\mathbb{F}^{1+t_{\operatorname{ood},i}+t_{i}}$  is a zero-evader with error  $\varepsilon_{\operatorname{zero},i}$ ;
  - $-\operatorname{ze}_{\operatorname{ood},i} \colon D_{\operatorname{ood},i} \to \mathbb{F}^{t_{\operatorname{ood},i} \times (\ell_i + \ell_{\operatorname{zk}})} \text{ is a zero-evader with error } \varepsilon_{\operatorname{ood},i};$
- $t_{\mathfrak{n}}, t_{\mathsf{zk}} \in \mathbb{N};$
- set  $k_{\mathfrak{n}} \coloneqq 0$ , and assume  $2^{k_{\mathfrak{i}+1}} \cdot \ell_{\mathfrak{i}+1} \ge \ell_{\mathfrak{i}}$  for every  $\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]$ ;
- set  $K_j := \sum_{i \leq j} k_i$ ,  $N_i := n + K_i$  and  $(K, N) := (K_{n-1}, N_{n-1})$ .

There exists an IOPP for  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_{1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{1}}},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}_{0}}$  with the following properties.

- Round complexity:  $K + 3 \cdot (\mathfrak{n} 1) + 2$  rounds.
- Prover communication (in field elements):

$$\sum_{\mathbf{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} \left( k_{\mathbf{i}} \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}}) + 1 + 2^{k_{\mathbf{i}+1}} \cdot m_{\mathbf{i}+1} \cdot \iota_{\mathbf{i}+1} + m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} + t_{\mathsf{ood},\mathbf{i}} \right)$$

$$+m_{\mathfrak{n}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{n}} + N \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} + \ell_{\mathfrak{n}} + r_{\mathfrak{n}} + N \cdot (\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + r_{\mathsf{zk}}).$$

Of these:

{62}------------------------------------------------

- $(N + \sum_{i \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} k_i) \cdot m_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot \iota_{\mathsf{zk}} \text{ are sent as an oracle over alphabet } \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{N + \sum_{i \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} k_i},$
- $\forall i \in [\mathfrak{n}-1], \ 2^{k_{i+1}} \cdot m_{i+1} \cdot \iota_{i+1} \ are \ sent \ as \ oracles \ over \ alphabet \ (\Sigma_{i+1})^{2^{k_{i+1}}},$
- $-m_{\mathfrak{n}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{n}}$  are sent as an oracle over alphabet  $\Sigma_{\mathfrak{n}}$ ,
- $-\sum_{\mathfrak{i}\in[\mathfrak{n}-1]}\left(k_{\mathfrak{i}}\cdot\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}+t_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}+1\right)+\ell_{\mathfrak{n}}+r_{\mathfrak{n}}+N\cdot(\ell_{\mathsf{zk}}+r_{\mathsf{zk}})\ are\ sent\ as\ non-oracle\ messages.$
- Query complexity:  $\sum_{i \in [n]} t_i + N \cdot t_{zk}$  oracle queries in total.
- Prover time (in field operations):

$$O\left(\ell_1 \cdot 2^{k_1} + t_{\mathsf{sl}} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + \sum_{\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} \left( \begin{array}{c} \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathfrak{i}}+1}}) + k_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) \\ + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}_{\mathfrak{i}}) + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}) \\ + \mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}}}^{\#}, t_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{i}}) + \mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}}}^{\$}, t_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{i}}) \end{array} \right) + \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}) + N \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}) \right).$$

• Verifier time (in field operations):

$$O\left(t_{\odot_{K}\mathsf{sl}} + \sum_{i \in [n]} t_{\mathsf{sl}_i} + \sum_{\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} \left(\begin{array}{c} k_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \ell_{\mathsf{zk}} + \mathsf{teval}(\mathsf{ze}_{\mathfrak{i}}) \\ + \mathsf{b}(\odot_{K-K_{\mathfrak{i}}} \mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}}}^{\#}, t_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{i}}) + \mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}}}^{\$}, t_{\mathfrak{i}} \cdot \iota_{\mathfrak{i}}) \\ + \mathsf{b}(\odot_{K-K_{\mathfrak{i}}} \mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}^{\leftarrow}}, t_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}) + \mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathsf{ze}_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}^{\rightarrow}}, t_{\mathsf{ood},\mathfrak{i}}) \end{array}\right) + \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}) + N \cdot \mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}})\right).$$

• Round-by-round security: For every  $\delta_{\mathsf{zk}} \in (0,1)$  and  $(\delta_{\mathsf{i}})_{\mathsf{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}]} \in (0,1)^{\mathfrak{n}}$ , the protocol has RBR knowledge soundness with relaxation  $\tilde{\mathcal{R}}^{\delta_1,\delta_{\mathsf{zk}}}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}_0}$  with the errors  $\epsilon_{\mathsf{cs},1} \| \cdots \| \epsilon_{\mathsf{cs},\mathfrak{n}-1} \| \epsilon_{\mathsf{base}}$  defined below and total extraction time

$$O\left(\sum_{\mathfrak{i}\in[\mathfrak{n}-1]}\left(\sum_{h\in[k_{\mathfrak{i}}]}\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathfrak{i}}-h}})+\mathsf{tenc}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{i}})\right)+\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}})+N_{\mathfrak{n}-1}\cdot\mathsf{tcor}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}})\right)\,.$$

- For every  $i \in [n-1]$ , define

$$\boldsymbol{\epsilon}_{\mathsf{cs,i}} \coloneqq \left( \begin{array}{l} \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{i}}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathsf{i}}}}, \delta_{\mathsf{i}})| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv N_{\mathsf{i}}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \\ \frac{\left(\epsilon_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{i}}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathsf{i}}-h}}, \delta_{\mathsf{i}}) + \frac{\ell_{\mathsf{zk}} \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{i}}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathsf{i}}-(h-1)}}, \delta_{\mathsf{i}})| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv N_{\mathsf{i}}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|} \right)_{h \in [k_{\mathsf{i}}]}, \\ \frac{\left(|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathsf{i}}+1}}, \delta_{\mathsf{i}+1})| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|\right)^{2}}{2} \cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{ood,i}}, \\ \left(1 - \delta_{\mathsf{i}})^{t_{\mathsf{i}}}, \\ |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathsf{i}+1}}}, \delta_{\mathsf{i}+1})| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv N_{\mathsf{i}+1}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})| \cdot \varepsilon_{\mathsf{zero,i}} \end{array} \right),$$

- Define

$$\boldsymbol{\epsilon}_{\mathsf{base}} \coloneqq \left( \begin{array}{l} \boldsymbol{\epsilon}_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}, \delta_{\mathfrak{n}}) + \boldsymbol{\epsilon}_{\mathsf{mca}}(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv N}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}}) + \frac{|\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}^{\equiv 2}, \delta_{\mathfrak{n}})| \cdot |\Lambda(\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}^{\equiv 2 \cdot N_{\mathfrak{n}-1}}, \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})|}{|\mathbb{F}|}, \\ \max \left\{ (1 - \delta_{\mathfrak{n}})^{t_{\mathfrak{n}}}, (1 - \delta_{\mathsf{zk}})^{t_{\mathsf{zk}}} \right\} \end{array} \right).$$

- Zero-knowledge: Suppose that  $char(\mathbb{F}) \neq 2$ ,  $\ell_{zk} \geq 2$ , and:
  - for every  $i \in [n-1]$ ,  $ze_{ood,i}$  is a  $(\ell_{zk} r_i, \zeta_{ze,i})$ -private zero-evader;
  - for every  $i \in [2, \mathfrak{n}]$ ,  $C_i$  has a  $t_i$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{C_i}$ ;
  - $-\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}$  has a  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$ -query zero-knowledge encoding with error  $\zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ . Then the protocol is honest-verifier zero-knowledge with error

$$\sum_{\mathbf{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} \left( \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathbf{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathbf{i}+1}}}} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze},\mathbf{i}} + (k_{\mathbf{i}}+1) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \right) + \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}} + N \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$$

and simulator query complexity  $(t_1, (t_{zk})_{i \in [n]})$ .

{63}------------------------------------------------

*Proof.* Let  $\mathfrak{sl}_0$  be the initial tuple from the theorem statement and for each  $\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]$  let  $\mathfrak{sl}_{\mathfrak{i}}$  be the output tuple after stage  $\mathfrak{i}$ . For each  $\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]$ , apply Theorem 9.10 with

$$(\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}', n, k, t, t_{\text{ood}}) = \left(\mathcal{C}_{\mathbf{i}}, \mathcal{C}_{\mathbf{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathbf{i}+1}}}, N_{\mathbf{i}-1}, k_{\mathbf{i}}, t_{\mathbf{i}}, t_{\text{ood}, \mathbf{i}}\right)$$

and with zero-evaders  $ze_i$  and  $ze_{ood,i}$ , obtaining an IOR IOR<sub>i</sub> from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_i^{\equiv 2^{k_i}}, N_{i-1}, \mathcal{C}_{zk}, sl_{i-1}}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_{i+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{i+1}}}, N_{i-1}, \mathcal{C}_{zk}, sl_{i}}$ . Then  $IOR_{cs} \coloneqq IOR_1 \circ \cdots \circ IOR_{\mathfrak{n}-1}$  is an IOR from  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_1^{\equiv 2^{k_1}}, \mathcal{C}_{zk}, sl_0}$  to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_n, \mathcal{C}_{zk}, sl_{n-1}}$ .

Apply the IOPP  $\mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{base}}$  from Theorem 7.1 to  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}_{\mathfrak{n}-1}}$  with  $n \coloneqq N, t \coloneqq t_{\mathfrak{n}}$ , and  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  as in the statement. The final IOPP for  $\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{p}}^{\equiv 2^{k_1}},\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}_0}$  is  $\mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{cs}} \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{base}}$ .

The stated round/query/communication/time bounds and the round-by-round error vector (including extraction time) follow by careful accounting. We focus on establishing zero knowledge.

**Zero-knowledge.** We establish HVZK for all distinguishers by building simulators  $\mathbf{S}_{\mathfrak{n}}, \mathbf{S}_{\mathfrak{n}-1}, \ldots, \mathbf{S}_{1}$ , and applying Theorem 4.5 at each step. For each stage  $\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]$ , define

$$\epsilon_{i} \coloneqq \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{i+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{i+1}}}} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze},i} + (k_{i}+1) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}.$$

Also define tail-error terms: for  $s \in [\mathfrak{n}]$ ,  $E_s := (\sum_{\mathfrak{i}=s}^{\mathfrak{n}-1} \epsilon_{\mathfrak{i}}) + \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}} + N \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ ; for  $s = \mathfrak{n}$  the sum is empty, so  $E_{\mathfrak{n}} = \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}} + N \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}$ .

- Base case. Let  $S_n$  be the simulator for  $IOR_{base}$  from Theorem 7.1; the simulator has error  $E_n$  and queries the main oracle at most  $t_n$  times and each of the N mask oracles at most  $t_{zk}$  times. As  $IOR_{base}$  is an IOPP, simulation works (trivially) for all distinguishers.
- Inductive step (i = n-1 down to 1). Suppose we have already constructed a simulator  $S_{i+1}$  for the IOPP  $IOR_{i+1} \circ \cdots \circ IOR_{n-1} \circ IOR_{base}$  that has simulation error  $E_{i+1}$  and that queries the  $C_{i+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{i+1}}}$ -oracle at most  $t_{i+1}$  times and each of the  $N_i$  mask oracles at most  $t_{zk}$  times.

Fix any distinguisher  $\mathcal{D}$  and let  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}}$  be as in Definition 4.4, i.e.,  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}}^{\mathbf{y}}(\cdot) := \mathbf{S}_{i+1}^{\mathbf{y}}(\cdot)$ . By the query bounds of  $\mathbf{S}_{i+1}$ ,  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}}$  queries the  $\mathcal{C}_{i+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{i+1}}}$ -oracle at most  $t_{i+1}$  times and each of the  $N_i$  output mask oracles at most  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  times; so  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}} \in \mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t_{i+1},(t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{j\in[N_i]})}$ . Thus  $\mathfrak{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}} \subseteq \mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t_{i+1},(t_{\mathsf{zk}})_{j\in[N_i]})}$ .

The IOR IOR<sub>i</sub> from Theorem 9.10 (instantiated with  $n = N_{i-1}$  input masks) is HVZK with respect to  $\mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t_{i+1},(t_{zk})_{j\in[N_i]})}$ : the  $k_i$  mask oracles introduced during the sumcheck phase are each queried by  $\mathcal{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}}$  at most  $t_{zk}$  times (since they belong to the  $N_i$  output masks), satisfying  $t_{N_{i-1}+j} \leq t_{zk}$  for every  $j \in [k_i]$  as required. Since  $\mathfrak{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}} \subseteq \mathfrak{D}^{\leq (t_{i+1},(t_{zk})_{j\in[N_i]})}$ , IOR<sub>i</sub> is in particular HVZK with respect to  $\mathfrak{D}_{\mathbf{S}_{i+1}}$ .

Let  $\mathbf{S}_{i}$  be simulator from Theorem 9.10, with error  $\epsilon_{i}$  and query complexity at most  $t_{i}$  to the  $C_{i}^{\equiv 2^{k_{i}}}$ -oracle and at most  $t_{zk}$  to each of the  $N_{i-1}$  input mask oracles. Applying Theorem 4.5 with  $\mathsf{IOR}_{1} \coloneqq \mathsf{IOR}_{i}$  (simulator  $\mathbf{S}_{i}$ ) and  $\mathsf{IOR}_{2} \coloneqq \mathsf{IOR}_{i+1} \circ \cdots \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{n-1} \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{base}}$  (simulator  $\mathbf{S}_{i+1}$ ) yields a simulator for the IOPP  $\mathsf{IOR}_{i} \circ (\mathsf{IOR}_{i+1} \circ \cdots \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{n-1} \circ \mathsf{IOR}_{\mathsf{base}})$  that is HVZK with ZK error  $\epsilon_{i} + E_{i+1} = E_{i}$ .

• Conclusion. Unrolling the induction to i = 1 gives a simulator  $\mathbf{S} := \mathbf{S}_1$  for the full protocol.  $\mathbf{S}$  queries the original implicit instance  $(f, (\xi_i)_{i \in [n]})$  at most  $t_1$  times for f and at most  $t_{\mathsf{zk}}$  times for each  $\xi_i$ , as guaranteed by Theorem 9.10 for stage 1. The total ZK error is  $E_1$ , which equals

$$\sum_{\mathbf{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]} \left( \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathbf{i}+1}^{\equiv 2^{k_{\mathbf{i}+1}}}} + \zeta_{\mathsf{ze},\mathbf{i}} + (k_{\mathbf{i}}+1) \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}} \right) + \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathfrak{n}}} + N \cdot \zeta_{\mathcal{C}_{\mathsf{zk}}}.$$

{64}------------------------------------------------

**Efficiency.** The efficiency of the construction follows by accumulating the costs of the building blocks throughout, and computing the cost of succinct linear form at each step (in particular, the codeswitches costs in see Section 9.3). The latter add the following terms to the prover/verifier time — the prover needs to compute a batch of size  $t_i \cdot \iota_i$  of the linear forms  $\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_i}^\#, \mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_i}^\$$  for all  $\mathfrak{i} \in [\mathfrak{n}-1]$ , as this must be proved by subsequent reductions. Similarly, the verifier must compute the (folded) succinct linear forms associated with those codeswitches, which entails  $\mathsf{b}(\odot_{K-K_i}\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_i}^\#, t_{\mathfrak{i}}) + \mathsf{b}(\mathsf{sl}_{\mathcal{C}_i}^\$, t_{\mathfrak{i}})$  field operations (as these are also computable in a batch).

{65}------------------------------------------------

#### <span id="page-65-0"></span>11 Zero-knowledge reduction from R1CS

We describe a reduction from  $\mathcal{R}_{R1CS}$  to testing proximity to a constrained code relation, similar to the one in Definition 5.8. The reduction is similar to the  $\Sigma$ -IOP from |ACFY25|, combined with a masking technique similar to the one used for the zero-knowledge sumcheck in Section 6.

#### Definition 11.1. Let:

- $n_{\rm in}, n_{\rm out} \in \mathbb{N};$
- $\mathcal{C} \subseteq \mathbb{F}^m$  with a zero-knowledge encoding  $\mathsf{Enc}_{\mathcal{C}} \colon \mathbb{F}^\ell \times \mathbb{F}^r \to \Sigma^m$ ;
- $C_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \ with \ a \ zero-knowledge \ encoding \ \mathsf{Enc}_{C_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}};$
- $C_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}} \subseteq \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \ with \ a \ zero-knowledge \ encoding \ \mathsf{Enc}_{C_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \colon \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \times \mathbb{F}^{r_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} \to \Sigma_{\mathsf{zk}}^{m_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}}};$
- $\bullet \quad \mathbf{sl} \ = \ (\mathbf{sl}, (\mathbf{sl}_i^{\mathrm{in}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{in}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}, (\mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}) \quad where \ \mathbf{sl} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_i^{\mathrm{in}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{zk}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{in}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{2 \times \ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{zk}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathrm{out}}}|, \ \mathbf{sl}_{\circ,i}^{\mathrm{out}} \ \in \ \langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathrm{out}} \rangle \rangle$  $\langle \mathbb{F}^{\ell_{\text{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}}} |$

Define:

$$\mathcal{R}_{\mathcal{C},\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{in}}^{\mathsf{zk}},\mathcal{C}_{\mathrm{out}}^{\mathsf{zk}},\mathsf{sl}} \coloneqq \left\{ \begin{array}{l} & \left( (\mu,\mathsf{st},(\mathsf{st}_{i}^{\mathsf{in}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}), \\ & ((\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{in}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{in}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}), \\ & ((\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}), \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{in}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}})_{i \in [n_{\mathrm{out}}]}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}}, \\ & (\mu_{i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}},\mathsf{st}_{\circ,i}^{\mathsf{out}}, \\ &
